PREFACE
   This code of the City of St. Maries, as supplemented, contains ordinances up
to and including ordinance 2025-784, passed March 24, 2025. Ordinances of the
City adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of this code to the
extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith. Consult the City
office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision of the code has
been amended, superseded or repealed.
American Legal Publishing
Cincinnati, Ohio
ORDINANCES PENDING REVIEW FOR CODIFICATION
Listed ordinances have been passed, but they are pending review by the
publisher, and they may not amend the code of ordinances. Additionally,
ordinances listed in this section may not show the original ordinances in their
entirety. Please contact the office of the clerk if there are any questions
concerning any listed ordinances.
 
TITLE 1
ADMINISTRATION
CHAPTER 1
ST. MARIES CITY CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Title
1-1-2: Authority
1-1-3: Acceptance
1-1-4: Amendments
1-1-5: Code Alterations
1-1-1: TITLE:
Upon adoption by the city council, this city code is hereby declared to be and
shall hereafter constitute the official city code of St. Maries. This city code
of ordinances shall be known and cited as the ST. MARIES CITY CODE and is
hereby published by authority of the city council and shall be supplemented to
incorporate the most recent legislation of the city as provided in section
1-1-4 of this chapter. Any reference to the number of any section contained
herein shall be understood to refer to the position of the same number, its
appropriate chapter and title heading, and to the general penalty clause
relating thereto, as well as to the section itself, when reference is made to
this city code by title in any legal documents. (2004 Code)
1-1-2: AUTHORITY:
This code consists of all the regulatory and penal ordinances and certain of
the administrative ordinances of the city codified pursuant to the provisions
of Idaho Code 50-903 through 50-906. (1977 Code § 1.01.060; amd. 2004 Code)
1-1-3: ACCEPTANCE:
The city code, as hereby presented in printed form, shall hereafter be received
without further proof in all courts and in administrative tribunals of this
state as the ordinances of the city of general and permanent effect, except the
excluded ordinances enumerated in section
1-2-1 of this title. (2004 Code)
1-1-4: AMENDMENTS:
   A.   Ordinance: Any ordinance amending the city code shall set forth the
title, chapter and section number of the section or sections to be amended, and
this shall constitute sufficient compliance with any statutory requirement
pertaining to the amendment or revision by ordinance of any part of this city
code.
   B.   Codification: All such amendments or revisions by ordinance shall be
immediately forwarded to the codifiers, and the ordinance material shall be
prepared for insertion in its proper place in each copy of this city code. Each
such replacement page shall be properly identified and shall be inserted in
each individual copy of the city code. (2004 Code)
   C.   Reference: Whenever a reference is made to this code or to any portion
thereof, or to any ordinances of the city, the reference shall apply to all
amendments, corrections and additions heretofore, now or hereafter made. (1977
Code § 1.01.070; amd. 2004 Code)
1-1-5: CODE ALTERATIONS:
It shall be deemed unlawful for any person to alter, change, replace or deface
in any way any section or any page of this city code in such a manner that the
meaning of any phrase or order may be changed or omitted. Replacement pages may
be inserted according to the official instructions when so authorized by the
city council. The city clerk shall see that the replacement pages are properly
inserted in the official copies maintained in the office of the city clerk. Any
person having custody of a copy of the city code shall make every effort to
maintain said code current as to the most recent ordinances passed. Such person
shall see to the immediate insertion of new or replacement pages when such are
delivered or made available to such person through the office of the city
clerk. Said code books, while in actual possession of officials and other
interested persons, shall be and remain the property of the city and shall be
returned to the office of the city clerk when directed so to do by order of the
city council. (2004 Code)
CHAPTER 2
SAVING CLAUSE
SECTION:
1-2-1: Repeal Of General Ordinances
1-2-2: Public Ways And Public Utility Ordinances
1-2-3: Reference To Specific Ordinances
1-2-4: Court Proceedings
1-2-5: Severability Clause
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES:
   A.   Prior Ordinances: All general ordinances of the city passed prior to
the adoption of this code are hereby repealed, except such as are included in
this code or are by necessary implication herein reserved from repeal (subject
to the saving clauses contained in the following sections), and excluding the
following ordinances which are not hereby repealed: tax levy ordinances;
appropriation ordinances; ordinances relating to boundaries and annexations;
franchise ordinances and other ordinances granting special rights to persons or
corporations; contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a
contract or the issuance of warrants; salary ordinances; ordinances
establishing, naming or vacating streets, alleys or other public places;
improvement ordinances; bond ordinances; ordinances relating to elections;
ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by or from the
city; and all special ordinances. (2004 Code)
   B.   Continuations; Conflicting Ordinances: The ordinances in this code, so
far as their provisions are substantially the same as those of previously
existing ordinances, must be construed as continuations thereof, and not as new
enactments; any ordinances previously adopted in conflict with the ordinances
set out herein are repealed, subject to the provisions of Idaho Code 50-905.
(1977 Code § 1.01.010)
   C.   Effect Of Repeal: The repeal of ordinances as provided in subsection B
of this section shall not affect any right which has accrued, any duty imposed,
any penalty incurred, nor any action or proceeding commenced under or by virtue
of the ordinances repealed, nor the tenure of office of any person holding
office at the time when they take effect; nor shall the repeal of any ordinance
thereby have the effect of reviving any ordinance heretofore repealed or
superseded. (1977 Code § 1.01.020; amd. 2004 Code)
1-2-2: PUBLIC WAYS AND PUBLIC UTILITY ORDINANCES:
No ordinance relating to railroad crossings with streets and other public ways,
or relating to the conduct, duties, service or rates of public utilities shall
be repealed by virtue of the adoption of this code or by virtue of the
preceding section, excepting as this code may contain provisions for such
matters, in which case, this code shall be considered as amending such
ordinance or ordinances in respect to such provisions only. (2004 Code)
1-2-3: REFERENCE TO SPECIFIC ORDINANCES:
The provisions of this code shall not in any manner affect matters of record
which refer to, or are otherwise connected with ordinances which are therein
specifically designated by number or otherwise and which are included within
this code, but such reference shall be construed to apply to the corresponding
provisions contained within this code. (1977 Code § 1.01.090)
1-2-4: COURT PROCEEDINGS:
   A.   Prior Acts: No new ordinance shall be construed or held to repeal a
former ordinance whether such former ordinance is expressly repealed or not, as
to any offense committed against such former ordinance or as to any act done,
any penalty, forfeiture or punishment so incurred, or any right accrued or
claim arising under the former ordinance, or in any way whatever to affect any
such offense or act so committed or so done, or any penalty, forfeiture or
punishment so incurred or any right accrued or claim arising before the new
ordinance takes effect, save only that the proceedings thereafter shall conform
to the ordinance in force at the time of such proceeding, so far as
practicable. If any penalty, forfeiture or punishment may be mitigated by any
provision of a new ordinance, such provision may be, by consent of the party
affected, applied to any judgment announced after the new ordinance takes
effect.
   B.   Extend To All Repeals: This section shall extend to all repeals, either
by express words or implication, whether the repeal is in the ordinance making
any new provisions upon the same subject or in any other ordinance.
   C.   Current Pending Actions: Nothing contained in this chapter shall be
construed as abating any action now pending under or by virtue of any general
ordinance of the city herein repealed, and the provisions of all general
ordinances contained in this code shall be deemed to be continuing provisions
and not a new enactment of the same provisions; nor shall this chapter be
deemed as discontinuing, abating, modifying or altering any penalty accrued or
to accrue, or as affecting the liability of any person, firm or corporation, or
as waiving any right of the city under any ordinance or provision thereof in
force at the time of the adoption of this code. (2004 Code)
1-2-5: SEVERABILITY CLAUSE:
If any section, subsection, subdivision, paragraph, sentence, clause or phrase
of this code or any part thereof or any portion adopted by reference therein is
for any reason held to be unconstitutional or invalid or ineffective by any
court of competent jurisdiction, such decision shall not affect the validity or
effectiveness of the remaining portions of this code, or any part thereof or
any portion adopted by reference therein. The city council hereby declares that
it would have passed each section, subsection, subdivision, paragraph,
sentence, clause or phrase thereof irrespective of the fact that any one or
more sections, subsections, subdivisions, paragraphs, sentences, clauses or
phrases be declared unconstitutional, invalid or ineffective. (2004 Code)
CHAPTER 3
DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
1-3-1: Rules Of Construction
1-3-2: Definitions
1-3-3: Catchlines
1-3-1: RULES OF CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   Title Of Office: Use of the title of any officer, employee, department,
board or commission means that officer, employee, department, board or
commission of the city. (1977 Code § 1.04.020)
   B.   Interpretation Of Language: All words and phrases shall be construed
according to the common and approved usage of the language, but technical words
and phrases and such others as may have acquired a peculiar and appropriate
meaning in the law shall be construed and understood according to such peculiar
and appropriate meaning. (1977 Code § 1.04.030)
   C.   Grammatical Interpretation: The following grammatical rules shall apply
unless it is apparent from the context that a different construction is
intended:
      1.   Gender: A word importing either the masculine or feminine gender
only shall extend and be applied to the other gender and to persons.
      2.   Singular And Plural: The singular number includes the plural and the
plural includes the singular.
      3.   Tenses: Words used in the present tense include the past and the
future tenses and vice versa, unless manifestly inapplicable. (1977 Code §
1.04.040; amd. 2004 Code)
   D.   Acts By Agents: When an act is required by this code, the same being
such that it may be done as well by an agent as by the principal, such
requirement shall be construed to include all such acts performed by an
authorized agent. (1977 Code § 1.04.050; amd. 2004 Code)
   E.   Prohibited Acts Include Causing And Permitting: Whenever in this code
any act or omission is made unlawful, it shall include causing, allowing,
permitting, aiding, abetting, suffering or concealing the fact of such act or
omission. (1977 Code § 1.04.060; amd. 2004 Code)
   F.   Computation Of Time: Except when otherwise provided, the time within
which an act is required to be done shall be computed by excluding the first
day and including the last day, unless the last day is Sunday or a holiday, in
which case it shall also be excluded. (1977 Code § 1.04.070)
   G.   Construction: The provisions of this code and all proceedings under
them are to be construed with a view to effect their objects and to promote
justice. (1977 Code § 1.04.080; amd. 2004 Code)
1-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and phrases, whenever used in this code, shall be construed
as defined in this section unless from the context a different meaning is
intended or unless a different meaning is specifically defined and more
particularly directed to the use of such words or phrases:
AGENT: A person acting on behalf of another with authority conferred, either
expressly or by implication.
CITY: The city of St. Maries, Idaho, or the area within the territorial limits
of the city of St. Maries, Idaho, and such territory outside the city over
which the city of St. Maries has jurisdiction or control by virtue of any
constitutional or statutory provision.
CITY COUNCIL: The city council of the city. "All its members" or "all
councilmen" means the total number of council members holding office.
CODE: The city code of the city of St. Maries.
COUNTY: The county of Benewah.
EMPLOYEE: Whenever reference is made in this code to a city employee by title
only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of the city of
St. Maries".
FISCAL YEAR: The financial year of the city beginning on October 1 of each year
and ending on September 30 of the following year.
INFRACTION: A civil public offense, not constituting a crime, punishable by a
penalty not exceeding one hundred dollars ($100.00) and for which no
incarceration may be imposed 1 .
LAW: Denotes applicable federal law, the constitution and statutes of the state
of Idaho, the ordinances of the city of St. Maries and, when appropriate, any
and all rules and regulations which may be promulgated thereunder.
LICENSE: The permission granted for the carrying on of a business, profession
or occupation.
MAY: May is permissive.
MISDEMEANOR: Any offense not defined as a felony or infraction under state law
2 .
MONTH: The calendar month.
MUST, SHALL: "Must" and "shall" are each mandatory.
NUISANCE: Anything offensive to the sensibilities of reasonable persons, or any
act or activity creating a hazard which threatens the health and welfare of
inhabitants of the city, or any activity which, by its perpetuation, can
reasonably be said to have a detrimental effect on the property of a person or
persons within the community.
OATH: Includes an affirmation or declaration in all cases in which, by law, an
affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and in such cases the words "swear"
and "sworn" shall be equivalent to the words "affirm" and "affirmed".
OCCUPANT: As applied to a building or land, shall include any person who
occupies the whole or any part of such building or land, whether alone or with
others.
OFFENSE: Any act forbidden by any provision of this code or the omission of any
act required by the provisions of this code.
OFFICERS: Whenever reference is made in this code to a city officer by title
only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of the city of
St. Maries".
OPERATOR: The person who is in charge of any operation, business or profession.
OWNER: As applied to a building or land, includes any part owner, joint owner,
tenant in common, joint tenant, tenant by the entirety, or lessee of the whole
or a part of such building or land.
PERSON: A natural person, joint venture, joint stock company, partnership,
association, club, company, corporation, business, trust, organization, or the
manager, lessee, agent, servant, officer or employee of any of them.
PERSONAL PROPERTY: Includes every description of money, goods, chattels,
effects, evidence of rights in action and all written instruments by which any
pecuniary obligation, right or title to property is created, acknowledged,
transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished and every right or
interest therein.
PRECEDING AND FOLLOWING: Next before and next after, respectively.
PROPERTY: Includes real and personal property.
REAL PROPERTY: Includes lands, tenements and hereditaments.
RETAILER: Unless otherwise specifically defined, shall be understood to relate
to the sale of goods, merchandise, articles or things direct to the customer.
RIGHT OF WAY: The privilege of the immediate use of the roadway or other
property.
SIDEWALK: That portion of a street between the curbline and the adjacent
property line intended for the use of pedestrians.
STATE: The state of Idaho.
STREET: Includes all streets, highways, avenues, lanes, alleys, courts, places,
squares, curbs, or other public ways in the city which have been or may
hereafter be dedicated and open to public use, or such other public property so
designated in any law of this state.
TENANT AND OCCUPANTS: Applied to a building or land, include any person who
occupies the whole or a part of such building or land, whether alone or with
others.
WHOLESALER: The terms "wholesaler" and "wholesale dealer" as used in this code,
unless otherwise specifically defined, shall be understood to relate to the
sale of goods, merchandise, articles or things to persons who purchase for the
purpose of resale.
WRITTEN; IN WRITING: May include printing and any other mode of representing
words and letters, but when the written signature of any person is required by
law to any official or public writing or bond, it shall be in proper
handwriting of such person, or in case such person is unable to write, by such
person's proper mark.
YEAR: The fiscal year of the city, October 1 through September 30 of the
following year. (1977 Code § 1.04.010; amd. 2004 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. IC §§ 18-111 and 18-113A; see subsection 1-4-1B of this title.
2 1. IC §§ 18-111 and 18-113; see subsection 1-4-1A of this title.
1-3-3: CATCHLINES:
The catchlines of the several sections of this code are intended as mere
catchwords to indicate the content of the section and shall not be deemed or
taken to be titles of such sections, nor be deemed to govern, limit, modify or
in any manner affect the scope, meaning or intent of the provisions of any
section hereof, nor unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when
any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or reenacted. (2004
Code)
CHAPTER 4
GENERAL PENALTY
SECTION:
1-4-1: General Penalty
1-4-2: Application Of Provisions
1-4-3: Liability Of Officers
1-4-1: GENERAL PENALTY 1 :
   A.   Misdemeanor: Unless specifically provided elsewhere, any person
convicted of a violation of any section or provision of this code deemed a
misdemeanor may be fined in a sum not to exceed one thousand dollars
($1,000.00) for any offense and may be confined in the county jail for a period
of not more than six (6) months. Either or both such fine and imprisonment may
be imposed; and in addition thereto, any person so convicted shall pay such
costs as the court may assess.
   B.   Infraction: When the offense is designated as an infraction by any
section or provision of this code or by state law, it is punishable only by a
penalty not exceeding one hundred dollars ($100.00) and no incarceration may be
imposed 2 .
   C.   Federally Mandated Programs: Any city which is participating in a
federally mandated program, wherein penalties or enforcement remedies are
required by the terms of participation in the program, may enforce such
requirements by ordinance, to include a criminal or civil monetary penalty not
to exceed one thousand dollars ($1,000.00), or imprisonment for criminal
offenses not to exceed six (6) months or to include both a fine and
imprisonment for criminal offenses. (2004 Code; amd. Ord. 2023-766, 3-27-2023)
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 50-302.
2 2. IC § 18-113A.
1-4-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Application Of Penalty Provisions:
      1.   The penalty provided in this chapter shall be applicable to every
section of this code the same as though it were a part of each and every
separate section. Any person convicted of a violation of any section of this
code where any duty is prescribed or obligation imposed or where any action
which is of a continuing nature is forbidden or is declared to be unlawful
shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor unless otherwise provided. A separate
offense shall be deemed committed upon each day such duty or obligation remains
unperformed or such act continues unless otherwise specifically provided in
this code.
      2.   Whenever the doing of any act or the omission to do any act
constitutes a breach of any section or provision of this code, and there shall
be no fine or penalty specifically declared for such breach, the provisions of
this chapter shall apply.
   B.   One Recovery For Same Offense: In all cases where the same offense is
made punishable or is created by different clauses or sections of this code,
the prosecuting officer may elect under which to proceed, but not more than one
recovery shall be had against the same person for the same offense; provided,
that the revocation of a license or permit shall not be considered a recovery
or penalty so as to bar any other penalty being enforced. (2004 Code)
1-4-3: LIABILITY OF OFFICERS:
No provision of this code designating the duties of any officer or employee
shall be so construed as to make such officer or employee liable for any fine
or penalty provided for a failure to perform such duty unless the intention of
the city council to impose such fine or penalty on such officer or employee is
specifically and clearly expressed in the section creating the duty. (2004
Code)
CHAPTER 5
CORPORATE AND OFFICIAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
1-5-1: City Boundaries
1-5-2: Corporate Seal
1-5-3: City Elections
1-5-4: Official Newspaper
1-5-1: CITY BOUNDARIES:
   A.   Legal Description On File: The boundaries and corporate limits of the
city, including all annexed territory, whether heretofore or hereafter annexed,
shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk at city hall, the same to
constitute the official boundaries and corporate limits of the city. (1977 Code
§ 1.12.010)
   B.   Territory Subject To Jurisdiction: All of the territory bounded and
described and included within the legal description of the city kept on file at
the office of the city clerk is declared and ordained to be within the
corporate limits of the city, and to be constituted the territory subject to
the jurisdiction of the city. (1977 Code § 1.12.020; amd. 2004 Code)
1-5-2: CORPORATE SEAL 1 :
   A.   Design: The corporate seal of the city shall be circular in form with
inner and outer circles. It shall bear upon the space between the two (2)
circles the words "City of St. Maries, Benewah Co., Idaho," and upon the space
within the inner circle the words, "Corporate Seal". (1977 Code § 1.16.010;
amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Adopted: The seal described in subsection A of this section is adopted
as the seal of the city. (1977 Code § 1.16.020; amd. 2004 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 50-301.
1-5-3: CITY ELECTIONS:
   A.   Hours Of Polling Places: The polls for all general and special city
elections shall be open from twelve o'clock (12:00) noon, Pacific time, and
remain open until eight o'clock (8:00) P.M., Pacific time. (Ord. 637, 9-8-2003)
1-5-4: OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER:
The St. Maries Gazette Record, a newspaper in and of general circulation in the
city, is hereby established as the official newspaper of the city. (2004 Code)
CHAPTER 6
MAYOR
SECTION:
1-6-1: Qualifications And Election
1-6-2: General Powers And Duties
1-6-1: QUALIFICATIONS AND ELECTION:
The mayor shall be a qualified elector of the city, and shall be elected for a
term of four (4) years. (2004 Code)
1-6-2: GENERAL POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Preside At Meetings: It shall be the duty of the mayor to preside at
all meetings of the city council.
   B.   Voting: The mayor shall have a casting vote when the city council is
equally divided.
   C.   Supervisory Control: The mayor shall have a supervisory control over
all other officers and over the affairs of the city.
   D.   Ordinances: The mayor shall have power to veto or sign any ordinance
passed by the city council.
   E.   Communication With City Council: The mayor shall, from time to time,
communicate to the city council such information or recommend such measure as,
in his opinion, may improve, ornament or promote the general prosperity of the
city. (1977 Code § 2.08.020)
CHAPTER 7
CITY COUNCIL
SECTION:
1-7-1: City Council Members; Election
1-7-2: City Council Meetings
1-7-3: President Of The City Council
1-7-4: Order Of Business
1-7-5: Rules Of Procedure
1-7-6: Ordinances
1-7-7: Committees
1-7-1: CITY COUNCIL MEMBERS; ELECTION:
There shall be six (6) city council members, elected at large for four (4) year
terms, said terms to be staggered. (2004 Code)
1-7-2: CITY COUNCIL MEETINGS:
   A.   Regular Meetings: The official meetings of the city council are hereby
established as the second and fourth Mondays of each month beginning at the
hour of five thirty o'clock (5:30) P.M. (Ord. 2008-666, 9-22-2008)
   B.   Special Meetings: Special meetings of the city council may be called by
the mayor, or by one-half (1/2) plus one of the members of the full city
council, the object of which shall be submitted to the city council in writing
and the call and object, as well as the disposition thereof, shall be entered
upon the journal by the city clerk. (1977 Code § 2.04.020; amd. 2004 Code)
   C.   Presiding Officer:
      1.   Mayor: The mayor shall be the presiding officer of the city council
but he shall have no vote unless the city council is otherwise equally divided,
in which event he shall cast the deciding vote.
      2.   President: In the event of absence of the mayor, the president of
the city council shall be the presiding officer.
      3.   Temporary Presiding Officer: In the event of the absence of both the
mayor and the president of the city council, the city council shall appoint one
of their members as the temporary presiding officer. (1977 Code § 2.04.030)
   D.   Quorum: A quorum shall consist of a majority of the members of the city
council, and the city council shall be empowered to act if a quorum is present.
(1977 Code § 2.04.050)
1-7-3: PRESIDENT OF THE CITY COUNCIL:
   A.   Election: The president of the city council shall be elected by the
members of the city council at the first meeting after such election at which
members of the city council are elected. (1977 Code § 2.04.040)
   B.   Powers And Duties: The president of the city council shall have the
powers and perform the duties of the mayor in case of his absence or
disability; and, in case of vacancy in the office of mayor, until such vacancy
is filled. (1977 Code § 2.08.030; amd. 2004 Code)
1-7-4: ORDER OF BUSINESS:
When the city council shall have convened, the roll shall be called and all
absentees noted in the minutes of the city council. The regular order of
business shall be as follows:
   A.   Call meeting to order;
   B.   Approve minutes of previous meeting and city treasurer's report;
   C.   Unfinished business;
   D.   New business;
   E.   Report of committees;
   F.   Adjournment. (1977 Code § 2.04.060; amd. 2004 Code)
1-7-5: RULES OF PROCEDURE:
   A.   Presiding Officer, Powers And Duties: The presiding officer shall
preserve order and decorum, and may speak to points of order in preference to
other members; and shall decide all questions of order, subject to appeal to
the city council, on which appeal no member shall speak more than once without
permission of the city council. (1977 Code § 2.04.120)
   B.   Motions Under Debate: When a motion is under debate, no motion shall be
received except to adjourn, to lay on the table, to postpone to a day certain,
to refer, to amend or to postpone indefinitely; which several motions shall
have precedence in the order in which they are stated. (1977 Code § 2.04.130)
   C.   Motion For Adjournment: A motion for adjournment shall always be in
order, except when once put and voted down, the same shall not again be in
order until some other business shall have been taken up, and a motion to
adjourn shall always be decided without debate. (1977 Code § 2.04.140)
   D.   Voting: Every member who shall be present when the question is put
shall vote for or against the same, unless the city council shall excuse him;
but no member shall be permitted to vote on a question when the ayes and nays
are called for unless present when his name is called in regular order; except
that after having once voted, the member may change his vote if he so desires
at any time before the vote is announced by the presiding officer. (1977 Code §
2.04.150)
   E.   Consideration Of Motions: No motion shall be considered unless the same
shall be recorded. When a motion is recorded, it shall be stated by the
presiding officer before debate. It shall be reduced to writing if desired by
any member of the city council; but the mover may withdraw it at any time
before a decision or amendment is made to it. (1977 Code § 2.04.160)
   F.   Roll Call Vote: Upon a division of the city council, the names of those
voting for and those who voted against a question shall be entered upon the
journal when requested by the mayor or any member of the city council; and in
such case, it shall be the duty of the city clerk to enter on the journal the
names of the members so voting. (1977 Code § 2.04.170)
   G.   Majority Vote: All question, unless otherwise fixed by this chapter,
shall be determined by majority vote. (1977 Code § 2.04.180)
   H.   Suspension Of Rules: No standing rule or order of the city council
shall be suspended except by vote of two-thirds (2/3) of the members present;
nor shall the order of business established by the rules of the city council be
postponed or changed except by vote of two-thirds (2/3) of the members present;
and the ayes and nays of all present shall be recorded on any proposition to
suspend a rule. (1977 Code § 2.04.190)
   I.   Presiding Officer Permitted To Vote: A member of the city council
acting as presiding officer may vote on all questions presented to the city
council. (1977 Code § 2.04.200)
   J.   Alteration; Amendment: These rules and order of business may be
altered, amended or repealed only by two-thirds (2/3) vote of the whole city
council, and any member desiring to have the rules so altered, amended or
repealed, must give notice in writing at a previous meeting. (1977 Code §
2.04.210)
1-7-6: ORDINANCES:
   A.   Presentation: All proposed ordinances of the city shall be typewritten
or printed and presented to the city council by a member at any regular or
special meeting. (1977 Code § 2.04.070)
   B.   Readings:
      1.   Three Readings: Every proposed ordinance shall be read in meetings
of the city council on three (3) different days.
      2.   Discussion; Amendment; Referral To Committee: At each reading of an
ordinance, it shall be open to discussion and amendment and may be referred to
a committee and shall be passed to the next reading unless by vote at the
meeting some other disposition is made.
      3.   Final Passage: On final passage, the yeas and nays shall be called
and recorded and a concurrence of a majority of the whole number of members of
the city council shall be required for passage; provided, however, that three-
fourths (3/4) of the city council may dispense with the portions of this
section requiring all ordinances to be read on three (3) different days, and on
the vote upon the motion to dispense with the above provisions, the yeas and
nays shall be called and recorded. (1977 Code § 2.04.080)
   C.   Passage; Approval By Mayor:
      1.   Passage With Approval Of Mayor: When any proposed ordinance is
passed, it shall be signed by the city clerk, and the date of its passage by
the city council shall be added thereto, and it shall, within three (3) days
thereafter, be presented to the mayor, or, in case of his absence from the
city, to the president of the city council for his approval. If the proper
officer approves the same, he shall attach his signature thereto.
      2.   Failure Of Mayor To Sign: Should the mayor refuse or neglect to sign
such ordinance and return the same with his objection in writing at the next
regular meeting after the same has been presented to him, it shall become a law
without his signature. The city clerk shall annex to such ordinance a
certificate to the effect that the mayor has failed to sign or veto the same,
and it has therefore become a law without his signature. (1977 Code § 2.04.090)
   D.   Veto By Mayor; Council Reconsideration:
      1.   Veto: Should the mayor not approve the ordinance, he shall, before
the next regular meeting after such ordinance is presented to him for his
approval, return the same to the city council with his objections to the same
in writing.
      2.   Reconsideration: When any ordinance is so returned by the mayor, it
shall be reconsidered by the city council at the first regular meeting
thereafter.
      3.   Passage Notwithstanding Veto: If, on such reconsideration, two-
thirds (2/3) of the members elected to the city council shall vote in the
affirmative, the ordinance shall become a law notwithstanding the mayor's veto.
The city clerk, in such case, shall annex a certificate to the ordinance
stating that the same was vetoed by the mayor and that, on its reconsideration,
it received the required majority of votes. (1977 Code § 2.04.100)
   E.   Recording: It shall be the duty of the city clerk to safely keep the
original ordinances, after final passage, as permanent records of the city.
(1977 Code § 2.04.110; amd. 2004 Code)
1-7-7: COMMITTEES:
Upon the organization of the city council at the first Monday in January
following an election, it shall be the duty of the mayor to appoint the
following committees of the city council, consisting of three (3) members each,
as follows:
Administration committee, which shall study, review and report to the city
council on city matters relating to budget, finances, personnel, building code
and inspections, police.
Public works committee, which shall study, review and report to the city
council on city matters relating to streets, water, sewer, public grounds,
parks and cemetery, timber. (Ord. 2014-692, 2-10-2014)
CHAPTER 8
CITY OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES
SECTION:
1-8-1: Officers Designated
1-8-2: Term Of Office
1-8-3: Compensation
1-8-1: OFFICERS DESIGNATED:
The elected officers of the city are a mayor and six (6) council members,
including the council president. In addition and with the consent of the city
council, the mayor shall appoint a city clerk, city treasurer, city attorney,
public works director and such other officers as may be deemed necessary for
the efficient operation of the city. (Ord. 2017-714, 1-9-2017)
1-8-2: TERM OF OFFICE:
The term of office of all officers of the city shall commence on the second
Monday of January. (1977 Code § 2.08.170; amd. 2004 Code)
1-8-3: COMPENSATION:
Commencing on January 1, 2002, the salaries of the mayor and city council
members shall be as follows:
   A.   Mayor: The mayor shall receive an annual salary in the sum of six
thousand dollars ($6,000.00), payable at five hundred dollars ($500.00) per
month.
   B.   Council Members: Each member of the city council shall receive an
annual salary of three thousand dollars ($3,000.00), payable at two hundred
fifty dollars ($250.00) per month. (Ord. 628, 8-13-2001; amd. 2004 Code)
ARTICLE A. CITY CLERK
SECTION:
1-8A-1: General Powers And Duties
1-8A-1: GENERAL POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Attend Meetings; Record Proceedings: The city clerk shall attend all
meetings of the city council and keep a correct journal of its proceedings and
shall also keep a book or record of all ordinances of the city in which all of
the ordinances adopted by the city council and approved by the mayor, or which
may be adopted without his approval, together with the proof of their
publication, shall be recorded in regular order. He shall keep an index of such
book or ordinances and journal of proceedings.
   B.   Custody Of Records, Corporate Seal: The city clerk shall have the
custody of all the records of the city council, and of the corporate seal.
   C.   Additional Duties: The city clerk shall perform such other duties as
may be prescribed by ordinance or fixed by the laws of the state. (1977 Code §
2.08.040; amd. 2004 Code)
ARTICLE B. CITY TREASURER
SECTION:
1-8B-1: General Powers And Duties
1-8B-2: Deposit Of City Monies
1-8B-1: GENERAL POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Custodian Of Funds: The city treasurer shall be the custodian of all
monies that belong to the city.
   B.   Separate Accounts: The city treasurer shall keep a separate account of
each fund or appropriation, and debits and credits belonging thereto.
   C.   Receipts: The city treasurer shall give to every person paying any
money into the treasury a receipt therefor, showing the date of the payment,
and on what account paid.
   D.   Financial Records:
      1.   Bonds: The city treasurer shall keep a record of all outstanding
bonds against the city, showing the number, amount and date of each, to whom
issued and when paid or canceled. (1977 Code § 2.08.070; amd. 2004 Code)
      2.   Books: The city treasurer shall keep a complete set of double entry
books; and enter therein everything appertaining to the finances of the city,
distributed in their respective funds, showing the amount appropriated and
expended for each particular item or appropriation, according to estimation of
the administration committee, and shall furnish a complete trial balance at the
first meeting of the city council of each month, reporting at the same time the
balance remaining in each fund. (1977 Code § 2.08.070; amd. 2004 Code; Ord.
2014-692, 2-10-2014)
   E.   Reports To City Council: The city treasurer shall, at the first of each
month and as often as may be required, render to the city council, under oath,
an account showing the state of the treasury at the date of such account, and
the balance on hand.
   F.   Failure To Report; Vacancy: A failure on the part of the city treasurer
for the space of ten (10) days after demand, or from the end of each month, to
render such account, shall be cause for the city council to declare his office
vacant, and they may fill such vacancy by appointment until the next election.
(1977 Code § 2.08.070; amd. 2004 Code)
   G.   Utility Payments: It shall be the duty of the city treasurer, in the
event of the failure of a water consumer of the city to make payments at the
time and in the manner prescribed by the ordinances of the city, to enforce the
same by directing and ordering the water of delinquent water users turned off,
and to also issue necessary orders for the turning on of the water when the
water users have complied with the rules and regulations of the city and have
paid the delinquent bill as prescribed in the ordinances of the city. (1977
Code § 2.08.060)
1-8B-2: DEPOSIT OF CITY MONIES:
The city treasurer may be required to keep all money in his hands belonging to
the city at such place or places of deposit within the city as approved by
ordinance of the mayor and city council. (1977 Code § 2.08.080; amd. 2004 Code)
ARTICLE C. CITY ATTORNEY
SECTION:
1-8C-1: Duties And Responsibilities
1-8C-1: DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES:
   A.   Legal Advisor: The city attorney shall be the legal adviser of the city
council.
   B.   Suits; Actions: The city attorney shall commence, prosecute and defend
all suits and actions necessary to be commenced, prosecuted or defended on
behalf of the corporation, or that may be ordered by the city council. (1977
Code § 2.08.100)
   C.   Attend Meetings: The city attorney may attend all regular meetings of
the city council and give them his opinion on any matter submitted to him
either orally or in writing. (1977 Code § 2.08.100; amd. 2004 Code)
   D.   Additional Duties: The city attorney shall perform such other duties as
may be required of him by ordinance. (1977 Code § 2.08.100)
ARTICLE D. PUBLIC WORKS DIRECTORS
SECTION:
1-8D-1: Powers And Duties
1-8D-1: POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Supervisory Control: The directors of public works, subject to orders
of the mayor and city council, shall have supervisory control over all street
improvements and the construction of all sidewalks. (1977 Code § 2.08.160; amd.
2004 Code)
   B.   Repairs: It shall be the duty of the public works directors to see that
all defects in the streets and sidewalks are repaired immediately on notice of
the same; provided, however, that this shall not authorize him to construct new
walks or grade new streets, except by order of the city council. (1977 Code §
2.08.160)
ARTICLE E. BUILDING INSPECTOR
SECTION:
1-8E-1: Appointment Or Contract
1-8E-2: Powers And Duties
1-8E-1: APPOINTMENT OR CONTRACT:
The city council and county commissioners shall appoint a building inspector
for the city, or the city council may elect to joint contract with the county
for building inspector services. (1977 Code § 15.08.010; amd. 2004 Code)
1-8E-2: POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Authority: The building inspector shall have authority to ensure
compliance with title 9 of this code and all existing ordinances pertaining to
building codes within the city.
   B.   Building Permits; Inspections: The building inspector shall have
authority to issue permits for and cause inspection of said structures in
accordance with the ordinances of the city; to collect permit fees according to
the adopted schedule of the city and county and to account for and pay to the
county all such fees, such payment and accounting to be made at least once each
month.
   C.   Stop Work Orders: The building inspector shall have the power to issue
stop work orders for noncompliance with title 9 of this code or with the
building codes adopted by the city. (1977 Code § 15.08.020; amd. 2004 Code)
TITLE 2
BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS
CHAPTER 1
PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION
SECTION:
2-1-1: Title
2-1-2: Definitions
2-1-3: Commission Established
2-1-4: Officers
2-1-5: Powers And Duties
2-1-6: Rules, Record And Meetings
2-1-7: City Officials To Cooperate
2-1-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the CITY PLANNING AND ZONING
COMMISSION. (1977 Code § 2.32.010)
2-1-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms, phrases, words, and their
derivations shall have the meaning given herein:
APPOINTIVE MEMBERS: All members of the commission.
COMMISSION: The planning and zoning commission hereby created.
GOVERNING BOARD: The city council of the city of St. Maries, Benewah County,
Idaho. (1977 Code § 2.32.020)
2-1-3: COMMISSION ESTABLISHED:
   A.   Established: A planning and zoning commission is established in and for
the city.
   B.   Composition: The commission shall consist of five (5) members,
including at least one member who shall reside within the city impact area
pursuant to Idaho Code 67-6526. All members must have resided in the county for
at least two (2) years immediately preceding appointment to the commission. The
area of impact member(s) must have resided in the city or the area of impact
for at least two (2) years immediately preceding appointment to the commission
and must reside within the area of impact while serving on the commission. All
other members must have resided in the city for two (2) years immediately
preceding appointment to the commission, and must reside within the city while
serving on the commission.
   C.   Appointment: Members shall be appointed by the mayor and confirmed by
the city council.
   D.   Compensation: Compensation for members shall consist of reimbursement
for travel outside the limits of the city while on commission business at a
given rate per mile compensatory with city council policy.
   E.   Term: Two (2) members of the commission shall be appointed to serve
terms of three (3) years and three (3) commission members shall be appointed to
serve terms of four (4) years, with terms expiring on September 30. The city
council may, by resolution, designate or assign a three (3) year term or a four
(4) year term for each commission seat.
   F.   Vacancies: Vacancies in the commission shall be filled in the same
manner as the original appointments.
   G.   Removal: Members may be removed for cause by a majority vote of the
governing board.
   H.   Power To Incur Indebtedness: Neither the commission nor any member
thereof shall incur any financial liability in the name of the city except as
authorized by the mayor and city council. (1977 Code §§ 2.32.030, 2.32.050,
2.32.070, 2.32.140; amd. Ord. 2016-710, 7-24-2016; Ord. 2022-757, 6-20-2022)
2-1-4: OFFICERS:
   A.   Chair: A chair shall be selected by a majority vote of the members of
the commission.
   B.   Additional Offices: The commission may create and fill such additional
offices as it may determine necessary for the proper conduct of the affairs and
business of the commission.
   C.   Ex Officio Advisors: The commission may appoint nonvoting ex officio
advisors as may be deemed necessary. (1977 Code § 2.32.090)
2-1-5: POWERS AND DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the planning and zoning commission to:
   A.   Provide ways and means to obtain citizen participation in the
administration of title 11 of this code;
   B.   Prepare a procedure for processing zoning permits namely: special use
permits, rezone applications, planned unit development proposals and variance
applications;
   C.   Recommend changes in the city comprehensive plan to the governing
board;
   D.   Hear all requests for amendment to title 11 of this code, hold at least
one public hearing and make its recommendation to the governing board;
   E.   Recommend changes to title 11 of this code, if needed, to the governing
board; and
   F.   Make recommendations to governing board for changes to boundaries of
the city and to zoning areas included therein. (1977 Code § 2.32.120)
2-1-6: RULES, RECORD AND MEETINGS:
   A.   Rules; Bylaws: Written organization papers or bylaws consistent with
Idaho Code title 67, chapter 65 and other laws of the state for the transaction
of business of the commission shall be adopted.
   B.   Records: A record of meetings, hearings, resolutions, studies,
findings, permits and actions taken shall be maintained.
   C.   Meetings: All meetings and records shall be open to the public. At
least one regular meeting shall be held each month for not less than nine (9)
months in a year.
   D.   Quorum: A majority of voting members of the commission shall constitute
a quorum. (1977 Code § 2.32.110)
2-1-7: CITY OFFICIALS TO COOPERATE:
All officers and division heads of the city shall cooperate with the commission
and render all reasonable assistance. (1977 Code § 2.32.130)
TITLE 3
BUSINESS AND LICENSE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL BUSINESS LICENSES
(Reserved)
CHAPTER 2
LIQUOR CONTROL
SECTION:
3-2-1: Title
3-2-2: Purpose
3-2-3: Idaho Laws Adopted
3-2-4: Beer Regulations
3-2-5: Wine Regulations
3-2-6: Liquor Regulations
3-2-1: TITLE:
This chapter will be known as the LIQUOR CONTROL ORDINANCE of the city. (2004
Code)
3-2-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to protect the general health, safety and public
welfare of city residents and visitors by regulating the hours, places and
conditions for the sale of alcoholic beverages in the city. (2004 Code)
3-2-3: IDAHO LAWS ADOPTED:
There is adopted for the purpose of governing the licensing, sale and use of
alcoholic beverages within the city the laws of the state, being particularly
Idaho Code title 23, as presently in effect or as may hereafter be amended by
the Idaho legislature, the same adopted and incorporated as an ordinance of the
city as fully as though set forth at length herein. Copies of said laws shall
be kept on file in the office of the city clerk for use and examination by the
public. (Ord. 227, 1971)
3-2-4: BEER REGULATIONS:
   A.   Definitions:
   BEER: Shall be defined as provided in Idaho Code title 23, chapter 10, as
amended from time to time.
   RETAILER: Any person engaged in the sale or distribution of beer to the
consumer.
   B.   License Required: It is unlawful for any person to sell beer without
first obtaining a proper license.
   C.   Application For License:
      1.   Application for the retail sale of beer shall be made and filed with
the city clerk in such form and manner as provided herein. The application
shall provide for the name of the applicant, the location of the proposed
business, the information required to show that the applicant meets the
qualifications required by this chapter, and such other information as may be
prescribed and required by the governing body. At the time the application is
filed, the applicant shall also present a copy of a license to sell beer
obtained from the county.
      2.   All applications received by the city clerk shall be referred to the
city council for final approval.
      3.   Licenses will be for a period of no longer than one year and shall
expire at one o'clock (1:00) A.M. on the first day of the renewal month for a
state license as determined by the director of Idaho state police.
   D.   Qualifications: No retail license shall be issued to any applicant who
is not qualified under Idaho Code title 23, chapter 10, as the same may be
amended from time to time.
   E.   Fee For License: The fee for a license for the sale of beer shall be
established by resolution of the city council, and shall be consistent with the
limitations provided in Idaho Code title 23, chapter 10, as amended from time
to time.
   F.   Revocation Of License:
      1.   The city council shall retain the right at all times to revoke and
cancel any license.
      2.   If any licensee or employee of a business licensed to sell beer by
the drink violates any of the provisions of this chapter or is convicted of
violation of any of the provision of the laws of the state relating the sale of
alcoholic beverages, the city council is authorized to revoke the license
issued to the licensee; provided, however, that in the event it is brought to
the attention of the city council that a violation has taken place, before
revoking such license, the city council shall cause notice to be served upon
the licensee, setting forth in general terms the violation or violations
claimed to have been committed, and such notice shall provide a time for
hearing thereon by the city council, which date of hearing shall not be less
than five (5) days nor more than ten (10) days from the date of the service of
the notice, and upon or following the hearing, the city council, if they shall
find that the provisions of this chapter or the provisions of the laws of the
state have been violated, shall revoke such license theretofore issued, and no
refund of any unused portion of the license fee shall be made to the licensee.
      3.   A revocation by the state or the county of any license to sell any
alcoholic beverages shall automatically revoke the license issued by the city.
   G.   Restrictions:
      1.   It is unlawful sell or dispense beer to be consumed on the premises
at any times other than those allowed in Idaho Code title 23, chapter 10, as
amended from time to time.
      2.   No license shall be issued for the sale of beer upon premises in
locations where such sale is prohibited by Idaho Code title 23, chapter 10, as
amended from time to time.
   H.   Regulations: It is unlawful for any person to sell beer to any person
to whom the sale of the same is prohibited by the laws of the state. Any
violation of this section shall constitute a misdemeanor. Any such sale by any
person licensed to sell or a person working at a business licensed to sell one
or more beverages shall be considered cause for cancellation of such license or
licenses as such person may be issued.
   I.   Renewal Of License:
      1.   Application for renewal of a license to sell beer shall be on the
same form as the application for the initial license.
      2.   If all of the information provided by the licensee is the same in
the application for renewal as was provided in the initial application, renewal
of the license may be issued by the city clerk without the application being
referred to the city council. (2004 Code)
3-2-5: WINE REGULATIONS:
   A.   Definitions:
   RETAILER: Any person engaged in the sale or distribution of wine to the
consumer.
   WINE: Shall be defined as provided in Idaho Code title 23, chapter 13, as
amended from time to time.
   B.   License Required: It is unlawful for any person to sell wine without
first obtaining a proper license.
   C.   Application For License:
      1.   Application for the retail sale of wine shall be made and filed with
the city clerk in the same form and manner as a license to sell beer. At the
time the application is filed, the applicant shall also present a copy of a
license to sell wine obtained from the state.
      2.   All applications received by the city clerk shall be referred to the
city council for final approval.
      3.   Licenses will be for a period of no longer than one year and shall
expire at one o'clock (1:00) A.M. on the first day of the renewal month for a
state license as determined by the director of Idaho state police.
   D.   Qualifications: No retail license shall be issued to any applicant who
is not qualified under Idaho Code title 23, chapter 13, as the same may be
amended from time to time.
   E.   Fee For License: The fee for a license for the sale of wine shall be
established by resolution of the city council.
   F.   Revocation Of License: The city council shall retain the right at all
times to revoke and cancel any license, subject to the same rights to appeal as
set forth in subsection
3-2-4F of this chapter relating to a license to sell beer.
   G.   Hours Of Sale Restricted: Wine sold for consumption on licensed
premises may be sold only during the hours that beer can be sold pursuant to
the laws of the state. Wine sold by a retailer for consumption off the premises
of the retailer may be sold only during the hours that beer may be sold
pursuant to the laws of the state.
   H.   Regulations: The sale of wine is subject to the same regulations as set
forth in subsection
3-2-4H of this chapter relating to the sale of beer.
   I.   Renewal Of License: Renewal of a license shall be accomplished in the
same manner as provided in subsection
3-2-4I of this chapter relating to renewal of a beer license. (2004 Code)
3-2-6: LIQUOR REGULATIONS:
   A.   Definitions:
   LIQUOR: Shall be defined as provided in Idaho Code title 23, chapter 9, as
amended from time to time.
   RETAILER: Any person engaged in the sale or distribution of liquor to the
consumer.
   B.   License Required: It is unlawful for any person to sell liquor without
first obtaining a proper license.
   C.   Application For License:
      1.   Application for the retail sale of liquor shall be made and filed
with the city clerk in the same form and manner as a license to sell beer. At
the time the application is filed, the applicant shall also present a copy of a
license to sell liquor obtained from the state.
      2.   All applications received by the city clerk shall be referred to the
city council for final approval.
      3.   Licenses will be for a period of no longer than one year and shall
expire at one o'clock (1:00) A.M. on the first day of the renewal month for a
state license as determined by the director of Idaho state police.
   D.   Qualifications: No retail license shall be issued to any applicant who
is not qualified under Idaho Code title 23, chapter 9, as the same may be
amended from time to time.
   E.   Fee For License: The fee for a license for the sale of liquor shall be
established by resolution of the city council and shall be in conformance with
Idaho Code title 23, chapter 9, as amended from time to time.
   F.   Revocation Of License: The city council shall retain the right at all
times to revoke and cancel any license, subject to the right to the same rights
to appeal as set forth in subsection 3-2-4F of this chapter relating to a
license to sell beer.
   G.   Restrictions:
      1.   Liquor may be sold or given away on any licensed premises only
during the hours of sale allowed in Idaho Code title 23, chapter 9, as amended
from time to time.
      2.   No license shall be issued for the sale of liquor upon premises in
locations where such sale is prohibited by Idaho Code title 23, chapter 9, as
amended from time to time.
   H.   Regulations: The sale of liquor is subject to the same regulations as
set forth in subsection 3-2-4H of this chapter relating to the sale of beer.
   I.   Renewal Of License: Renewal of a license shall be accomplished in the
same manner as provided in subsection 3-2-4I of this chapter relating to
renewal of a beer license. (2004 Code)
CHAPTER 3
PEDDLERS, SOLICITORS AND CANVASSERS
SECTION:
3-3-1: Purpose
3-3-2: Definitions
3-3-3: License Requirements
3-3-4: License Suspension, Revocation Or Denial
3-3-5: Conditions Of License
3-3-6: Exemptions
3-3-7: Unlawful Conduct
3-3-8: Violation; Penalty
3-3-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to provide the citizens and inhabitants of the
city with the information relating to persons who peddle, solicit or canvass
within the city and to protect citizens from deceptive or dishonest practices.
(Ord. 638, 12-22-2003)
3-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
PEDDLER, SOLICITOR OR CANVASSER: Any person either as a principal or agent who
goes from place to place within the city or who, while not going from place to
place, sells from the back of a motor vehicle or other temporary location, and
who:
   A.   Sells, takes orders for or offers to sell any goods, wares, merchandise
or services, whether collecting in advance for such goods, wares, merchandise
or services or not; or
   B.   Seeks contributions or donations in goods or legal tender.
PERSON: Includes, but is not limited to, an individual, partnership,
corporation, limited liability corporation or other business entity, whether
for profit or not for profit for purposes of licensing. (Ord. 638, 12-22-2003)
3-3-3: LICENSE REQUIREMENTS:
It is unlawful for any person to act as a peddler, solicitor, or canvasser
within the city without first having obtained a license issued pursuant to this
chapter. Each individual going door to door must have his or her own license,
whether or not such individual is acting alone or on behalf of a business
entity or employer.
   A.   Application, Fees, Term And Limitations:
      1.   Filing Of Application: Persons seeking a license under this chapter
shall file a written application for such license with the city clerk on the
form provided by the city.
      2.   Term: Licenses provided for in this chapter shall be issued for a
period of one year, and may be renewed upon application made prior to the
expiration of the license.
      3.   Fees: Applicants for licenses shall pay fees for the original or
renewal license in an amount which is established from time to time by
resolution of the city council.
      4.   Issuance: Upon filing a completed application with the city clerk,
the city will have ten (10) business days to issue or deny the license.
Licenses may be issued by the city clerk with the approval of the mayor; or may
be denied by the city clerk for cause, notice of which shall be given in
writing, which notice shall state therein the reasons for the denial.
   B.   Contents Of Application: The application shall be sworn to by each
applicant and shall be accompanied by an application fee for each license. The
applicant shall provide the following information on the form provided by the
city:
      1.   Name, physical description and gender, social security number,
driver's license number and date and place of birth of the applicant;
      2.   Permanent home address, telephone number and local address and
telephone number of the applicant;
      3.   A brief description of the nature of the business and goods to be
sold or services to be performed;
      4.   If employed by another, the name and address of the employer;
      5.   The place of manufacture or production of goods to be offered for
sale, the present location of such goods and the proposed method of delivery;
      6.   A polaroid picture of the applicant seeking a license taken by the
applicant at the time of application, which shall show the head and shoulders
of the applicant in a clear and distinguishing manner;
      7.   A statement by the applicant as to any convictions of crimes,
misdemeanors or violations of municipal ordinances, the date, the nature of the
offense and the penalty assessed against the applicant;
      8.   A statement that a license, if granted, will not be used or
represented as an endorsement by the city for solicitations thereunder;
      9.   The applicant's Idaho state sales tax certificate or temporary sales
tax permit;
      10.   If a vehicle is to be used, a description of the vehicle including
the license number;
      11.   When food or other products for human consumption are to be sold, a
certification by the applicable health agency shall be required prior to
issuance of the license. (Ord. 638, 12-22-2003)
3-3-4: LICENSE SUSPENSION, REVOCATION OR DENIAL:
   A.   Cause Of Suspension, Revocation Or Denial: A license issued under this
chapter may be suspended or revoked or issuance may be denied for any of the
following causes:
      1.   Fraud, misrepresentation or false statement contained in the
application for license;
      2.   Fraud, misrepresentation or false statement made in the course of
carrying on the business of being a peddler, solicitor or canvasser;
      3.   Any violation of this chapter, any violation of city ordinances or
carrying on business in violation of any city, state or federal law;
      4.   Conviction of any felony or other crime involving moral turpitude,
or conducting the business of peddling, soliciting or canvassing in an unlawful
manner or in such manner as to constitute a breach of the peace or so as to
constitute a menace to the health, safety or welfare of the public.
   B.   Notice: Notice of suspension, revocation or denial of a license shall
be in writing and mailed to the licensee at the address of record on the
original application.
   C.   Appeals: Any person aggrieved by the suspension, revocation or denial
of a license by the city clerk shall have the right of appeal to the city
council. Such appeal shall be taken by filing with the city clerk written
notice thereof within five (5) business days after the entry of the notice of
suspension, revocation or denial. The notice of appeal shall specify an address
at which the licensee may be given notice of hearing on the appeal. The city
council shall hear the appeal or may refer the same to a committee or hearing
examiner for hearing. The hearing will take place not more than fifteen (15)
business days from the date the notice off appeal is filed with the city clerk.
At the hearing, the licensee shall be entitled to appear in person and offer
evidence pertinent to the suspension, revocation or denial, or may appear
through legal counsel. The city clerk shall likewise be entitled to be heard at
the hearing and to offer evidence in support of the notice of suspension,
revocation or denial. The city council shall determine whether the suspension,
revocation or denial shall be upheld or reversed and shall put its findings and
conclusions in writing. At the discretion of the city council or hearing
examiner, other evidence may be received and other witnesses may be heard. A
transcribable record shall be retained relating to any hearing conducted. (Ord.
638, 12-22-2003)
3-3-5: CONDITIONS OF LICENSE:
   A.   Possession And Display Of License: The license shall be exhibited in a
conspicuous place if the licensee is using a vehicle or a building for the
conduct of business, or shall be in the possession of the licensee at all times
when peddling, soliciting or canvassing in the city and shall be exhibited by
said peddler, solicitor or canvasser whenever requested to do so by a peace
officer, the mayor, the city clerk or any person solicited or canvassed.
   B.   Hours Of Operation: All licensees may conduct business only between the
hours of eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. and eight o'clock (8:00) P.M. Monday through
Saturday. (Ord. 638, 12-22-2003)
3-3-6: EXEMPTIONS:
The licensing requirements of this chapter shall not apply to:
   A.   Newspaper carriers or sales persons whether subscriptions are taken or
not;
   B.   Any person licensed to do such business by the state;
   C.   Any person under the age of eighteen (18) years unless employed by
another person as defined in this chapter;
   D.   Any candidate or representative of a registered political committee;
   E.   Representatives of any charitable or nonprofit organization when the
solicitation is managed and conducted solely by officers and members of said
organizations who are unpaid for such services;
   F.   Occasional sales or fundraising efforts by local schools, university
student groups or local service clubs;
   G.   Commercial sales persons selling orders or soliciting orders for
wholesale businesses, retail businesses, local governments and schools.
   H.   The city, its agents and concessionaires;
   I.   Any bona fide auction sale;
   J.   Garage, yard or similar sales by individuals at their residence or
place of business, not exceeding three (3) days in length nor exceeding four
(4) sales in one calendar year, which sale shall not include business
inventory. (Ord. 638, 12-22-2003)
3-3-7: UNLAWFUL CONDUCT:
No licensee hereunder shall:
   A.   Make unwanted physical contact with the person being solicited;
   B.   Misrepresent the purpose of the solicitation;
   C.   Misrepresent the affiliation of those engaged in the solicitation;
   D.   Continue efforts to solicit from an individual once that individual
informs the solicitor that he does not wish to give anything or to buy anything
from that solicitor;
   E.   Represent that the issuance of any license issued under this chapter is
an endorsement or recommendation by the city;
   F.   Enter upon any premises when the same is posted with a sign stating "no
peddlers allowed" or "no solicitation allowed" or other words to such effect;
   G.   Knowingly make any false statement on an application for a license
hereunder;
   H.   Engage in any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement in the course
of carrying on the business. (Ord. 638, 12-22-2003)
3-3-8: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Violations of any provision of this chapter shall be unlawful and shall be an
infraction punishable by a civil penalty as provided in subsection 1-4-1B of
this code. Each calendar day that a violation continues shall constitute a
separate offense. (Ord. 638, 12-22-2003)
CHAPTER 4
FRANCHISES
SECTION:
3-4-1: Permit Or Franchise Required
3-4-2: Time Limit; Exclusivity Prohibited
3-4-3: Application
3-4-4: Objections
3-4-5: Granting Franchise
3-4-1: PERMIT OR FRANCHISE REQUIRED:
Any person who intends to construct or erect, or causes to be constructed or
erected, within the corporate limits of the city a cable television, electric
and/or gas system, whereby any part or portion of any highway, bridge, street
or alley in said corporate limits will be used for the erection of poles,
stretching of wires, laying underground wires or laying of pipes for purpose of
light plants, and laying water pipes for a system of waterworks, must first
obtain from the city council a permit or franchise. (1977 Code § 5.24.010; amd.
2004 Code)
3-4-2: TIME LIMIT; EXCLUSIVITY PROHIBITED:
No permit or franchise shall be granted for a longer period than twenty (20)
years, nor shall any permit or franchise be exclusive. (1977 Code § 5.24.020)
3-4-3: APPLICATION:
   A.   Contents: The application shall be presented to the city council and
shall state fully:
      1.   The persons, company, corporation or association applying for the
permit or franchise;
      2.   The object, purpose and period for which the permit is requested,
and the privileges asked for;
      3.   The designation of all highways, bridges, streets or alleys to be
made use of;
      4.   A full description of the mode of how the proposed line or system
and the extent of its plants, and how built, constructed or to be erected;
      5.   The proposed rates of tolls and charges to patrons and consumers,
and any concession in return for the permit to be made on the part of the
applicant to the city or its residents;
      6.   Any other information that will fully explain the terms, conditions,
and purposes under which the permit is requested. (1977 Code § 5.24.030)
   B.   City Council Action: After the filing of such application, the city
council shall cause an ordinance to be drawn up in conformity with the
application and also embodying therein such conditions, terms, regulations and
restrictions for the government, operation and construction of the respective
lines or systems as they deem fit. Such ordinance shall be read three (3) times
before final action is taken thereon. (1977 Code § 5.24.040)
   C.   Notice Of Application:
      1.   Publication Required: After the filing of any application for a
permit or franchise, the applicant shall, at his own expense, cause to be
published a notice that such application has been made, and in such notice
shall set forth the purpose, the period for which such permit or franchise is
requested, and the concessions, conditions and terms under which such permit or
franchise is requested. The highways, bridges, streets and alleys to be used in
the construction of the lines; or systems and the rate of tolls and charges
proposed to be charged to patrons and consumers shall be stated in the notice.
(1977 Code § 5.24.050)
      2.   Publication Requirements: Such notice shall be published in the
official newspaper of the city for a period of not less than four (4)
consecutive weeks. (1977 Code § 5.24.060)
3-4-4: OBJECTIONS:
Upon such notice being published, any resident of the city may file with the
city council any protest, remonstrance or objection against the granting of
such permit or franchise, such protest, remonstrance or objection to be in
writing and signed, and if the city council finds that a majority of the
property owners and taxable inhabitants in the city have signed such protest,
remonstrance or objection, such permit or franchise shall not be granted. (1977
Code § 5.24.070)
3-4-5: GRANTING FRANCHISE:
Should no majority of property owners and taxable inhabitants present protests,
remonstrances or objections, at the time when the ordinance for a permit or
franchise comes up for the third reading, such ordinance shall then come up for
final action, and it shall require a majority vote of members elected on the
city council to pass such ordinance. (1977 Code § 5.24.080; amd. 2004 Code)
CHAPTER 5
JUNKYARDS
SECTION:
3-5-1: Purpose
3-5-2: Definitions
3-5-3: License Requirements
3-5-4: Nuisances Declared
3-5-5: Violation; Penalty
3-5-1: PURPOSE:
For the purposes of promoting the public safety, health, welfare, convenience
and enjoyment of public travel, to protect the public investment in streets,
alleys, utilities, and to preserve and enhance the scenic beauty of the city,
it is declared by the city council to be in the public interest and for public
health and safety purposes to prohibit the establishment, operation and
maintenance of junkyards within the city. The city council finds and declares
that junkyards in the city are public nuisances. (Ord. 617, 11-8-1999)
3-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
JUNK: Old or scrap metal, wood, glass, plastic, rope, rags, batteries,
paper,trash, rubber, debris, waste; junk, inoperable, dismantled or wrecked
vehicles, boats or other machines or their parts.
JUNKYARD: A piece of real property which is maintained, operated or used for
storing, keeping, buying or selling junk, or for the maintenance or operation
of an automobile graveyard. (Ord. 617, 11-8-1999)
3-5-3: LICENSE REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Required: No person shall operate, establish or maintain a junkyard in
the city without first obtaining a license from the city council.
   B.   Issuance: Licenses may be granted by the city council for operation of
a junkyard or for storage otherwise in violation of this chapter when the city
council determines that the site meets the following requirements:
      1.   Is not a zoned residential area;
      2.   Does not unreasonably or adversely affect surrounding property
values or uses;
      3.   Does not unreasonably or adversely affect public use or enjoyment of
public streets, utilities or other public property; and
      4.   Does not present a significant health or safety concern.
   C.   License Term: Any license granted shall be for one calendar year
expiring December 31 and must be renewed by the city council after annual
reconsideration of the above criteria.
   D.   Fees: A shall be charged for each license or any renewed license and
shall be deposited with the city clerk. The amount of said fee shall be as
established by resolution of the city council, and amended from time to time.
   E.   Conditions Of License: The city council may condition or qualify any
license to limit permitted storage uses or require fencing or make other
reasonable requirements necessary to meet the requirements of this chapter.
(Ord. 617, 11-8-1999; amd. Ord. 2023-776, 12-21-2023)
3-5-4: NUISANCES DECLARED:
All violations of this chapter are hereby declared to be public nuisances. The
city may apply to the district court of Benewah County for an injunction
prohibiting further operation of any junkyard or dump in violation of this
chapter. (Ord. 617, 11-8-1999)
3-5-5: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person who knowingly allows a junkyard to exist in the city without a
license therefor, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished by a
fine not to exceed one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) and/or one hundred eighty
(180) days confinement in the county jail. Each calendar month in which the
violation continues shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord. 617, 11-8-1999)
TITLE 4
PUBLIC HEALTH AND SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
NUISANCES
SECTION:
4-1-1: Reserved
4-1-2: Declaration Of Nuisance; Acts Prohibited
4-1-3: Exceptions
4-1-4: Enforcement
4-1-5: Abatement
4-1-6: Request For Hearing
4-1-7: Open Burning
4-1-1: RESERVED:
(Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
4-1-2: DECLARATION OF NUISANCE; ACTS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any "responsible party(ies)" (defined as any person or
persons, corporation or other legal entity, tenant or lessee, landlord or
lessor using or occupying a premises) to cause, allow, maintain or permit the
existence of any nuisance on any property within the City of St. Maries. Any,
or all, responsible parties may be held accountable.
   A.   Keeping or permitting another to keep upon any premises deleterious or
septic material unless such material is retained in containers or vessels which
deny access to humans, flies, insects, rodents or other animals. Such materials
shall not be retained upon the premises for longer than twenty four (24) hours,
nor may such materials be regularly stored upon the premises even if exchanged
regularly with a new supply.
   B.   Permitting any premises to become a fire menace by allowing any dry or
dead grass, shrubs or other matter to grow, accumulate or otherwise occupy and
remain on such premises.
   C.   Permitting pools of water to accumulate and remain upon any premises
thereby becoming stagnant and foul.
   D.   Keeping or permitting another to keep upon any premises an accumulation
of trash, rubbish, garbage or other materials that attract or harbor
mosquitoes, flies, insects, rodents or other animals.
   E.   Keeping or permitting another to keep upon any premises an accumulation
of trash, rubbish, garbage or other materials, whether in containers or not,
which are fermenting, putrefying or odoriferous.
   F.   Keeping or permitting another to keep upon any premises an accumulation
of new or used appliances, new or used furniture not meant for outdoor use, or
other items that constitute an unsightly combination.
   G.   Keeping or permitting another to keep upon any premises an accumulation
of building materials that may attract children, rodents, or other animals.
Building materials being stored and used during construction upon the premises
shall be kept in a safe and secure manner and shall be removed from the
premises upon completion of construction.
   H.   Keeping or permitting another to keep upon any premises an accumulation
of automobile tires, wheels, parts or other items which may accumulate and
store stagnant water, or may attract insects, rodents, or other animals.
   I.   Keeping or permitting another to keep on any premises a "junked
vehicle" as defined by section
5-6-2 of this Code for a period of more than thirty (30) days.
   J.   Any act constituting a violation of section
5-6-3 of this Code.
   K.   Any other use of property which is specifically declared by resolution
of the Council to be a nuisance after compliance with the notice requirements
of this chapter.
   L.   Any partially destroyed or damaged house, building, trailer or other
structure or improvement to real property; and any partially constructed or
deconstructed house, building or other structure or real property improvement
upon which regular and daily progress is not being made to complete the
construction or deconstruction thereof; which constitutes a menace, threat or
hazard to the general health or safety of the community, including being an
attractive nuisance to minors.
   M.   Any house, building, trailer, structure or improvement to real
property, or any portion thereof, which, because of the condition thereof, is
found or permitted to be or remain a danger to the health, safety, life, limb
or property of any person entering into or around the same.
   N.   Any building, trailer, structure or improvement to real property, set
up, erected, constructed, altered, enlarged, converted, moved, or parked
contrary to the Building Codes or zoning ordinances of the City.
   O.   Any use of land, buildings or premises in violation of the zoning or
subdivision ordinances of the City.
   P.   The existence of any fence or other structure or item on private
property abutting any public street, sidewalk or place, which is in a sagging,
leaning, fallen, decayed, dilapidated or unsafe condition.
   Q.   Trees that are likely to fall and damage buildings or property owned by
another, or do injury to the life or property of another.
   R.   Any unguarded or abandoned excavation, pit or hole which would endanger
the safety of passersby.
   S.   Anything which unreasonably, or unlawfully interferes with, obstructs
or tends to obstruct, or renders dangerous for passage, any public or private
street, highway, sidewalk, stream, ditch, or drainageway.
   T.   Any condition or use of property which is detrimental to the health or
safety of persons or the property of others or which is declared to be a
nuisance by any Idaho State law, Federal laws or other provisions within this
Code. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
4-1-3: EXCEPTIONS:
Materials and things described in the foregoing section may be retained within
a building which prevents the view (or smell) of these things from the street
or from other public or private property. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018; amd. Ord.
2022- 760, 8-8-2022)
4-1-4: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Appointment: The Mayor, with the consent of the City Council, shall
appoint a duly authorized representative who shall be responsible for the
enforcement of this chapter. If no such "Code Officer" is formally appointed,
