any City police officer or the Benewah County Sheriff or one of his duly
constituted deputies and/or any authorized City employee or agent may serve as
such authorized representative.
   B.   Notice Of Violation: Written notice of a violation of this chapter
shall be served upon any adult occupying the real property upon which the
nuisance is located; or upon a responsible party; or upon the owner of such
real property, if known. If no occupant or other responsible party can be
located, then a written notice shall be affixed to any building on the subject
real property or posted to a place conspicuous on the property so as to be
reasonably discovered by anyone coming upon the real property. In the event
responsible parties are known, but have not been personally served a notice, in
addition to posting notice, the parties may be served by certified mail to
their last known mailing address. Any such notice shall constitute notice to
the owner and/or occupant of the real property.
   C.   Contents Of Notice: The notice of nuisance shall contain the following:
      1.   The physical address of the property where nuisance is located.
      2.   A general description of the nuisance.
      3.   The date of sending/posting the notice.
   D.   Penalty:
      1.   If the nuisance remains on the property longer than three (3) days
following notice of violation, it shall be an infraction and punishable as set
forth in the general penalty section (section
1-4-1 of this Code).
      2.   If the nuisance remains for more than ten (10) days following notice
of violation it will be a misdemeanor and punishable as set forth in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
      3.   In the event the nuisance remains for more than fifteen (15) days it
will be a separate misdemeanor violation for every day thereafter. (Ord. 2018-
723, 7-23-2018)
4-1-5: ABATEMENT:
   A.   Notice Of Abatement: The City may take action to have any such nuisance
abated. In such instance the notice of nuisance violation set forth in
subsection
4-1-4B of this chapter shall include a notice of abatement and such notice
shall include a provision that the expense of such abatement if not performed
on the property by the owner and/or the responsible party shall be assessed
against the real property involved pursuant to Idaho Code sections 50-334 and
50-1008. The notice shall also provide the responsible party and/or owner that
they may petition the City Council for hearing on the issue of abatement within
five (5) days of the posting/service of the notice.
   B.   Tolling Of Time Period: From the date a petition for hearing is filed
until five (5) days after a posthearing decision by the City Council the time
limit set forth in section
4-1-4 of this chapter shall be tolled.
   C.   Authority To Employ Labor: The Mayor is hereby given the power and
authority to employ such labor as is necessary to carry out the provisions of
this chapter. Any bills, costs or expenses incurred by the City (including
hourly wages of City employees), shall be assessed to the real property
pursuant to Idaho Code sections 50-334 and 50-1008. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
4-1-6: REQUEST FOR HEARING:
   A.   Request: Any person ordered to abate a nuisance may have a hearing with
the City Council as to whether a nuisance exists. A request for hearing must be
made in writing and delivered to the Office of the City Clerk within five (5)
days of the service or posting of the notice, or it will be conclusively
presumed that a nuisance exists and it must be abated as ordered.
   B.   City Council Decision: At the conclusion of the hearing, the City
Council shall render an oral decision to be memorialized in a written order as
to whether a nuisance exists. If it finds that a nuisance exists, it must be
ordered to be abated within additional time which must be reasonable under the
circumstances. Notice of the abatement order will be considered entered and
delivered as of the date of the City Council's oral pronouncement even though
written order is not signed by the Mayor until a later date. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-
23-2018)
4-1-7: OPEN BURNING:
   A.   Prohibited Zone: There is an established zone within the city where
there shall be no burning of trash or debris whatsoever at any time within the
year and said zone is described as follows:
From the north side of College Avenue to the west side of Eleventh Street to
the east side of Third Street; thence one block south to the north side of
Jefferson Avenue, and east to the east side of First Street; thence north to
the south side of Milwaukee Railroad; thence west to the west side of Eleventh
Street; thence south to the north side of College Avenue.
   B.   Permit Required: In other parts of the City not covered by the zone as
described in subsection A of this section, open burning requires a bum permit
from the St. Maries Fire Protection District. Applicable open burning
regulations established by the St. Maries Fire Protection District shall apply.
The use of portable, factory built, outdoor wood burning fireplaces or
permanently installed, outdoor wood burning fire pits for recreational fires
does not require a burn permit. Additionally, any structure used for outdoor
recreational fires that was not originally constructed to be used for wood
burning requires an inspection and approval by a fire code official or
designee. Once approved, that structure does not require a burn permit for a
recreational fire. Recreational fires must only bum clean, dry wood. Bum
barrels are prohibited. Burning is only permitted when the Idaho Department of
Environmental Quality (DEQ) has set the air quality level at GREEN. Burning
with YELLOW or RED air quality condition is prohibited. (Ord. 2019-730, 6-11-
2019; amd. Ord. 2022-754, 3-14-2022)
CHAPTER 2
FIREARMS
SECTION:
4-2-1: Title
4-2-2: Purpose
4-2-3: Definition
4-2-4: Discharge Prohibited
4-2-5: State Preemption
4-2-6: Violation; Penalty
4-2-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the FIREARMS DISCHARGE
ORDINANCE. (1977 Code § 8.24.010)
4-2-2: PURPOSE:
This chapter is enacted for the purpose of promoting the public safety by
reducing the hazards inherent by the discharge of firearms in a populated area.
(1977 Code § 8.24.020)
4-2-3: DEFINITION:
Whenever the term "firearm" is used in this chapter, the term shall mean any
instrument used in the propulsion of shot, shell or bullet or other harmful
objects by the action of gunpowder exploded within it. (1977 Code § 8.24.030)
4-2-4: DISCHARGE PROHIBITED:
   A.   Prohibited; Exception: It is unlawful to discharge any firearms within
the city, except at a regularly established shooting gallery; provided, that
this section shall not be construed to prohibit any officer of the law from
discharging a firearm in the performance of his duty, nor to any citizen from
discharging a firearm when lawfully defending person or property.
   B.   Tranquilizer Gun: This provision shall not apply to a veterinarian
discharging a tranquilizer gun in the performance of his occupation as a
veterinarian. (1977 Code § 8.24.040)
4-2-5: STATE PREEMPTION:
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to in any manner regulate the
ownership, possession or transportation of firearms when carried or transported
for purposes not prohibited by the laws of the state. (1977 Code § 8.24.050)
4-2-6: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person found guilty of violating any provision of this chapter shall be
deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. (1977 Code § 8.24.060)
CHAPTER 3
GARBAGE, RUBBISH AND REFUSE
SECTION:
4-3-1: Definitions
4-3-2: Contract For Services
4-3-3: Mandatory Use Required
4-3-4: Containers
4-3-5: Accumulation Prohibited
4-3-6: Littering Prohibited
4-3-7: Violation; Penalty
4-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
GARBAGE: All putrescible wastes except sewage and body wastes, including
vegetable and animal offal and carcasses of dead animals, but excluding
recognizable industrial byproducts, and shall include all such substances from
public and private establishments and from all residences.
REFUSE: All solid wastes including garbage and rubbish.
RUBBISH: Nonputrescrible wastes. (1977 Code § 8.12.010)
4-3-2: CONTRACT FOR SERVICES:
   A.   Authority: The mayor and city council may provide for the collection of
garbage, rubbish and refuse within the city and may contract for the collection
and disposal thereof with any qualified person lawfully engaged in the business
of collection and disposal of garbage or refuse in the St. Maries area. (1977
Code § 8.12.070)
   B.   Contract Required: No person shall collect, transport or dispose of
garbage or other refuse within the city limits who has not contracted with the
city to provide such service and who does not possess a license or franchise
from the city, and no person shall be granted such contract, permit or license
who is not capable of complying with the requirements of this chapter. (1977
Code § 8.12.080)
4-3-3: MANDATORY USE REQUIRED:
All premises including residence and business premises within the city shall be
required to subscribe to and make use of the garbage collection and disposal
system herein established. (1977 Code § 8.12.060)
4-3-4: CONTAINERS:
No owner, tenant or lessee of any public or private premises shall permit to
accumulate upon his premises any garbage or refuse except in covered containers
approved by the public works directors and shall abide by all rules and
regulations established by the city relating to the use and storage of said
containers. (1977 Code § 8.12.040; amd. 2004 Code)
4-3-5: ACCUMULATION PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person to permit or suffer to accumulate in or about any
yard, lot, place or premises or upon any street, alley or sidewalk adjacent to
such lot, yard, place or premises, owned or occupied by such person any garbage
or refuse so as to cause such yard, lot, premises to cause or create a nuisance
or offensive odor, atmosphere or rodent harborage or thereby be or become or
cause or create a public nuisance. (1977 Code § 8.12.100)
4-3-6: LITTERING PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person to throw or deposit in any street, alley,
sidewalk or footpath of the city any broken glass, bottles, crockery, nails or
other substance whatever whereby automobile tires or the feet of horses,
pedestrians or any beast of burden may be injured; or shall throw, deposit or
sweep into or upon any street, sidewalk or footpath of the city any paper or
other substance whatever. (1977 Code § 9.28.010; amd. 2004 Code)
4-3-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
It is unlawful and shall constitute a misdemeanor for any person to violate the
provisions of this chapter, or for any person to throw away, dump or discard
any type or nature of garbage or refuse on any public lands, rights of way or
private land belonging to another. Upon conviction of violation of this
chapter, the offender shall be punished as set forth in the general penalty in
section
1-4-1 of this code. In addition thereto, the court shall have power to issue an
injunction against further or continued violation of the terms or intent of
this chapter. (1977 Code § 8.12.110)
CHAPTER 4
WEEDS
SECTION:
4-4-1: Definitions
4-4-2: Destruction Required
4-4-3: Destruction By City, Charges
4-4-4: Authority To Employ Labor
4-4-5: Penalty
4-4-1: DEFINITIONS:
NOXIOUS WEEDS: All weeds and vegetable growth that have been declared noxious,
destructive and detrimental to agricultural interests. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-
2018)
4-4-2: DESTRUCTION REQUIRED:
   A.   Every person, either as owner, tenant, lessee or merely as occupant of
any lot, land or premises within the corporate limits of the City, shall, at
all times and continuously during the time and dates hereinafter stated,
destroy, cut down, weed out and obliterate all weeds, noxious weeds, grasses
and growths growing or starting to grow on any such lot, land or premises and
exceeding a height of eight inches (8").
   B.   Every person, during the time hereinafter stated, shall keep
continuously cut down, weeded out, destroyed and obliterated all weeds, noxious
weeds, grasses and growths from and off all that part or portion of land or
premises herein last referred to being the sidewalk around, as well as the
parking ground fronting, adjacent or contiguous to any such lots, lands or
premises.
   C.   All such weeds and noxious weeds, grasses and growths exceeding a
height of eight inches (8") which are deleterious, unsightly and injurious to
the public or to the residents or owners of adjacent property within the City
shall, at all times, continuously be kept weeded out, cut down, obliterated and
destroyed between May 31 and October 1 of each and every year. (Ord. 2018-723,
7-23-2018)
4-4-3: DESTRUCTION BY CITY, CHARGES:
   A.   Every person owning or occupying any lots, lands or premises situated
within the corporate limits of the City shall, within the time fixed by section
4-4-2 of this chapter, keep continuously destroyed, weeded out, cut down and
obliterated all such deleterious, unsightly and injurious weeds and noxious
weeds, grasses and growths exceeding a height of eight inches (8") in or on any
and all such lots, lands or premises so owned or occupied by such person in the
manner prescribed by and in accordance with the provisions of section
4-4-2 of this chapter.
   B.   In the event that such deleterious, unsightly and injurious weeds and
noxious weeds, grasses and growths are not so continuously destroyed, weeded
out, cut down and obliterated, the Mayor and City Council may cause, through
its duly authorized personnel, such deleterious, unsightly and injurious weeds
and noxious weeds, grasses and growths to be cut down, weeded out and
destroyed, and the costs and expenses of such destruction in cutting down,
weeding out and obliterating the same shall be assessed against such property,
as general taxes, and collectable as other general State, County and Municipal
taxes.
   C.   Before the costs and expenses of such destruction shall become a lien
against the property, the City Clerk is authorized and empowered to notify, in
writing, the owner of any such lot, place or area within the City, or the agent
of said owner, to cut, destroy and/or remove any such weeds, grasses or
deleterious, unhealthful growth or other noxious matter found growing, lying or
located on such property. The procedure set out in subsection 4-1-4B of this
title concerning abatement of nuisances shall be applicable to this chapter.
(Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
4-4-4: AUTHORITY TO EMPLOY LABOR:
The Mayor and City Council are hereby given the power and authority to employ
such labor as is necessary to carry out the provisions of this chapter. (Ord.
2018-723, 7-23-2018)
4-4-5: PENALTY:
   A.   Any person owning or occupying any lots, lands or premises within such
incorporated limits of the City who shall fail, refuse or neglect to
continuously keep weeded out, cut down, obliterated or destroyed all such
deleterious, unsightly and injurious weeds and noxious weeds, grasses and
growth above named in the manner prescribed and according to the provisions of
this chapter during the time provided for in section
4-4-2 of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of an infraction.
   B.   Each and every day any such person shall fail, refuse or neglect to
comply with the provisions of this chapter shall constitute a separate and
distinct offense against the provisions of this chapter, and each of such
separate offenses shall be punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
CHAPTER 5
VIDEO SURVEILLANCE POLICY
SECTION:
4-5-1: Benefit and Purpose
4-5-2: Application and Exceptions
4-5-3: Video System Placement
4-5-4: Authorized Use and Review
4-5-5: Inspection and Storage
4-5-1: BENEFIT AND PURPOSE:
   A.   Benefit: Benefit of the installation and use of video surveillance
systems can provide a visual deterrent to crime, assist with overall security
measures, and increase the potential identification and apprehension of person
(s) who breach City premises, use policies and/or commit criminal acts. The use
of security cameras extends the ability of the Administrative Staff when law
enforcement officers are not immediately available. Security cameras are not a
guarantee of safety; however, they do serve as deterrents and can alert
Administrative Staff to potential danger.
   B.   Purpose: The installation and use of video surveillance systems in
facilities, owned and/or possessed and occupied by the City shall facilitate
the following purposes:
      1.   The protection of the safety of City, employees, invitees who comply
with the City’s authorized public use in and around City Facilities; and
      2.   Respects the privacy rights of City employees and authorized invitee
use of City facilities; and
      3.   The primary use of surveillance cameras is to record images for
future identification of individuals and activity in the event of violations of
law or City policy. (Ord. 2021-750, 10-12-2021)
4-5-2: APPLICATION AND EXCEPTIONS:
   A.   Application: This policy regulates the use of surveillance cameras to
protect the legal and privacy interests of the City, its employees and
authorized invitee use of the City facilities. This policy applies to all City
use of surveillance systems and devices for monitoring and/or recording
activity.
   B.   Non-Surveillance Exceptions: This policy does not apply to the use of
video for non-surveillance purposes, examples include:
      1.   Cameras used for training and other related educational purposes.
      2.   Webcams used for purposes of communication between specific persons.
      3.   Cameras or camera systems use for virtual appearances at City
meetings.
      4.   Cameras or camera systems use for City promotional and or public
educational purposes.
   C.   Law Enforcement Exception: This policy does not apply to the use of
video surveillance systems for law enforcement purposes when used by or under
the direction of the Chief of Police. (Ord. 2021-750, 10-12-2021)
4-5-3: VIDEO SYSTEM PLACEMENT:
Video Surveillance cameras may be placed for the purposes of video monitoring
and recording of public places in accordance with the following:
   A.   The installation of new surveillance cameras, their locations, and
purpose must be approved in advance by the Mayor. Approval must be secured
prior to the purchase and installation of equipment.
   B.   Protection of individuals, including employees, administrative staff,
council members, independent contractors and authorized invitee use of City
facilities and the monitoring and recording pedestrian and vehicular traffic
activity.
   C.   Protection of buildings and property. Areas that may be monitored
include building perimeters, entrances and exits, lobbies, hallways and
corridors, training rooms, restricted access entrances to buildings, apparatus
bays and vehicle entrances and exits.
   D.   Verification of security alarms.
   E.   Monitor and record locations where intrusion alarms, security alarms
and exit door controls are installed.
   F.   Video monitoring of other public areas.
   G.   Video Surveillance cameras will not be placed in residential support
areas such as bathrooms and fitness spaces and in individual offices unless
they contain an exterior entrance to the facility.
   H.   Monitors for video equipment shall be installed in controlled-access
areas and shall not be viewable by unauthorized persons.
   I.   City Employees will be informed of the location of Video Surveillance
Cameras. (Ord. 2021-750, 10-12-2021)
4-5-4: AUTHORIZED USE AND REVIEW:
   A.   Authorization of Installation: Only the Mayor and the City Clerk or a
designee authorized by the Mayor or the City Clerk and approved by the City
Council, will be involved in, or have access to surveillance camera data unless
otherwise specifically ordered by the City Council (“Authorized Personnel”)
   B.   Ethics and Training: Video monitoring for security purposes will be
conducted in a professional, ethical and legal manner. Authorized Personnel
involved in active video monitoring will be trained and supervised in the
responsible use of this technology.
   C.   Not a Personnel Monitoring Tool: In general, the City will not permit
either the installation or use of cameras as a tool to monitor routine
performance or the use of personal “webcam” or similar technology for
surveillance purposes unless specifically ordered by the City Council pursuant
to a condition of a personnel action.
   D.   No Placebo Camera Placement: The placement and use of dummy or placebo
cameras is prohibited.
   E.   Authorized Image Review: When an incident is suspected to have
occurred, only Authorized Personnel may review the images from surveillance
camera data.
   F.   Surveillance Images Copying: Only the Mayor, the City Clerk or the City
Council may authorize copies of surveillance images.
   G.   Requests: All requests to release of surveillance records must be
authorized by the Mayor or the City Clerk pursuant to a property public records
request.
   H.   Release of Video Images: The Mayor and City Clerk have the
responsibility to evaluate and make decisions for the release of Recordings
based on the following request source criteria:
      1.   For legitimate investigative, safety and security reasons;
      2.   Law Enforcement agencies, where it is believed that the images will
assist in a legal inquiry;
      3.   Prosecuting agencies;
      4.   Legal Representatives via a subpoena;
      5.   The media, where a decision has been made that it is needed in order
to assist in the identification of victim(s), perpetrator(s) or witnesses in
relation to a criminal incident;
      6.   Otherwise required by law. (Ord. 2021-750, 10-12-2021)
4-5-5: INSPECTION AND STORAGE:
   A.   System Inspection: All authorized cameras and systems will be inspected
annually to ensure that they are in proper working condition and meet policy
guidelines.
   B.   Image Storage: Recorded camera images will be retained in accordance
with the storage capacity of the surveillance system and public record
retention requirements unless the Mayor or the City Clerk or the City Council
retain the camera images for an additional time. (Ord. 2021-750, 10-12-2021)
TITLE 5
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
POLICE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
5-1-1: Department Established
5-1-2: Appointment Of Police Chief
5-1-3: Chief Of Police
5-1-4: Members Of Department
5-1-5: Peace Officer Training
5-1-6: Assisting Officers
5-1-1: DEPARTMENT ESTABLISHED:
There is established a police department in the city which shall consist of a
chief of police, one assistant chief and such other police officers as the
needs of the department shall require. (1977 Code § 2.20.010)
5-1-2: APPOINTMENT OF POLICE CHIEF:
The mayor, with the consent of the city council, shall appoint the chief of
police of the city. (Ord. 2017-714, 1-9-2017)
5-1-3: CHIEF OF POLICE:
   A.   Powers And Duties:
      1.   Authority: The chief of police shall be subject to the orders of the
mayor and members of the city council;
      2.   Supervisory Control: The chief of police shall have supervisory
control over all other members of the police force;
      3.   Obstruction Of Streets Or Sidewalks; Nuisances: The chief of police
shall also notify the city council of any infringement of the ordinances
relating to the obstruction of streets, walks or sidewalks, by any person, and
of any nuisance that may come to his knowledge. (1977 Code § 2.08.130)
5-1-4: MEMBERS OF DEPARTMENT:
   A.   Supervision: All police officers shall be under the supervision of the
chief of police and subject to his orders. Members of the department shall also
be subject to the orders of the mayor. (1977 Code §§ 2.08.140, 2.20.030; amd.
2004 Code)
   B.   General Duties: It shall be the duty of police officers to preserve the
peace, restrain all riotous or disorderly conduct wherever the same occurs
within the city, remove all encroachments found upon the sidewalks, all
obstructions on the streets and to arrest all offenders and violators of the
laws and ordinances of the city. (1977 Code § 2.08.140)
   C.   Power, Duty To Arrest: In addition to other powers and duties provided
by ordinances and the statutes of the state, police officers shall have the
power and it shall be their duty to arrest or cause to be arrested and take
before the proper court all persons who shall break or threaten to break the
peace in the presence of such officer and to obtain a warrant for the arrest of
any person violating any ordinances of law out of the presence of such officer,
and the court may commit such persons to the county jail or other safe place in
default of bail being furnished. They or any of them shall have the power to
arrest all persons who shall be in the act of violating any ordinance of the
city or who may be reasonably suspected of committing any crime or of having
committed any crime or misdemeanor or of having violated any ordinance of the
city for the preservation of the peace and good order of the city. They shall
have power to detain or cause to be detained any person in custody in the
county jail or other safe place in the city for a reasonable period of time
until such person can be duly arraigned or tried by the proper officer. (1977
Code § 2.20.020)
   D.   Assistance To Other Officers: It shall be the duty of all officers and
members of the police department to aid and assist the chief of police and to
assist each other in the performance of police duties.
   E.   Service Of Warrant Or Process: While executing or serving or assisting
in the execution or service of any warrant or process, they shall be vested
with and have all the power and authority conferred by the laws of the state or
at common law. (1977 Code § 2.20.040)
5-1-5: PEACE OFFICER TRAINING:
   A.   Aid For Police Training: The city declares that it desires to qualify
to receive aid for police training from the law enforcement planning commission
under the provisions of Idaho Code 19-5110. (1977 Code § 2.24.010)
   B.   Adherence To State Standards: Pursuant to Idaho Code 19-5110, the city,
while receiving aid from the law enforcement planning commission, will adhere
to the standards for employment and training established by the Idaho peace
officer standards and training advisory council. (1977 Code § 2.24.020)
5-1-6: ASSISTING OFFICERS:
Any person in the city who shall be requested by the chief of police or any
officer or member of the police department to assist him in making an arrest,
capture or retaining in custody any person and shall refuse or fail to render
to the best of his ability such aid as is required shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor and on conviction be punished as set forth in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1977 Code § 2.20.050)
CHAPTER 2
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
5-2-1: Cruelty To Animals
5-2-2: Livestock
5-2-1: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
Any person who shall cruelly beat, torture, misuse, deprive of food and water,
or otherwise treat any animal with cruelty within the corporate limits of the
city shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished as set forth
in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1977 Code § 6.16.010)
5-2-2: LIVESTOCK:
It is unlawful for any person to keep any livestock of any kind within the
corporate limits of the city except for the keeping of chickens as provided in
section
11-5-10 of this code. (Ord. 2015-703, 6-8-2015)
ARTICLE A. DOGS
SECTION:
5-2A-1: Title
5-2A-2: Licensing
5-2A-3: Vaccinations
5-2A-4: Collars
5-2A-5: Running At Large
5-2A-6: Impoundment And License Check
5-2A-7: Public Nuisance
5-2A-8: Dogs In City Parks
5-2A-9: Penalty
5-2A-1: TITLE:
This article shall be known and may be titled as the ST. MARIES DOG ORDINANCE.
(Ord. 2019-729, 5-13-2019)
5-2A-2: LICENSING:
   A.   Required: All dogs present within the City must be licensed except:
      1.   Dogs quartered in a pet shop or shelter and held for resale or
adoption;
      2.   Dogs whose owners are temporarily (up to 30 days) within the City if
the dog's owner can produce evidence that the dog is currently licensed in
another jurisdiction or permanently resides in a jurisdiction that does not
require licensing;
      3.   Dogs under the age of six (6) months.
   B.   Application: License applications must be submitted to the City or the
City's authorized agent utilizing a standard form which requests name, address,
and telephone number of the applicant; breed, sex, color of the dog, and length
of license sought (up to 3 years).
   C.   Vaccination: The application must be accompanied by a rabies
vaccination certificate that will be valid for the full term of the license and
meets the requirements of section
5-2A-3 of this article.
   D.   Fee: The City or the City's authorized agent shall collect a fee for
each dog license in the amount established by resolution of the city council
and amended from time to time. Provided however, a fee will not be charged:
      1.   If the license is obtained during the month of January or any other
date range designated by the City Council as a fee licensing period.
      2.   For licensing a dog trained and used to assist government officials
in the performance of their duties that is owned by the government agency.
      3.   For renewal licenses of the same dog by the original licensee owner
upon expiration of the original license.
   E.   Renewal: The license will be valid for up to three (3) years from the
date of purchase, and may be renewed at no cost as set forth herein upon
application and vaccination certificate.
   F.   Tag: At the time of issuing the license, the City or the City's
authorized agent shall furnish and deliver to the party a license in the shape
of a metal tag, bearing the words "City of St. Maries" and the year for which
the same is issued stamped thereon. The person to whom the license is issued
shall cause the tag to be attached to a collar to be worn by the dog for which
the license was issued, during the time which the license is valid.
   G.   Replacement: A duplicate or replacement tag shall be issued by the City
or the City's authorized agent to replace the original tag which was lost or
destroyed. The fee for such replacement tags shall be as established by
resolution of the city council and amended from time to time. (Ord. 2019-729,
5-13-2019; amd. Ord. 2023-776, 12-21-2023)
5-2A-3: VACCINATIONS:
   A.   Required: Rabies vaccination is required for all dogs within thirty
(30) days of when the dog:
      1.   Reaches the age of three (3) months;
      2.   Is acquired or brought into the City if over three (3) months old;
or
      3.   The expiration of the most recent vaccination.
This provision shall not apply to veterinarian or kennel operators temporarily
maintaining on their premises animals owned by others.
   B.   Certificate: Each veterinarian, when vaccinating any dog for rabies,
shall complete a certificate of rabies vaccination (in duplicate) which
includes the following information:
      1.   Owner's name and address;
      2.   A description of animal (breed, sex, markings, age, name);
      3.   The date of vaccination;
      4.   The rabies vaccination tag number;
      5.   The type of rabies vaccine administered; and
      6.   The manufacturer's serial number of vaccine.
A copy of the certificate shall be distributed to the owner and the original
retained by the issuing veterinarian. (Ord. 2019-729, 5-13-2019)
5-2A-4: COLLARS:
   A.   Required: Except as otherwise provided in this article, every owner
shall be required to provide each dog with either a collar or harness to which
the license tag shall be attached and constantly worn by the dog.
   B.   Removal Prohibited: No person shall remove or cause to be removed the
collar or tag from any licensed dog without the consent of the owner, keeper or
harborer thereof.
   C.   Optional Microchip Or Tattooing: Every owner has the option, at his own
expense, of causing his dog to be microchipped or one of his dog's ears to be
permanently tattooed, and having the tattoo number recorded with the City or
the City's authorized agent. In such event the dog is not required to wear a
tag. (Ord. 2019-729, 5-13-2019)
5-2A-5: RUNNING AT LARGE:
   A.   Definition: "At large" is defined as any dog off the premises of a
person owning, harboring or keeping such dog and not under said person's
immediate care and control either by leash, cord, chain or otherwise without a
competent and responsible attendant.
   B.   Prohibited: No person owning, harboring, keeping or having in his
possession or under his control a dog, shall permit such dog to run at large.
(Ord. 2019-729, 5-13-2019)
5-2A-6: IMPOUNDMENT AND LICENSE CHECK:
   A.   Duty To Impound: It shall be the duty of the Sheriff or any suitable
person under his direction, to impound any dog running at large in violation of
the provisions of this article, and immediately notify the owner of such dog if
the owner's name is disclosed in the registry of licensed dogs or otherwise
known to the Sheriff that such dog has been impounded. If the owner cannot be
located or is not available to retrieve the dog, the dog shall be delivered to
the Benewah Humane Society and held in accordance with the Benewah Humane
Society policies and standards.
   B.   License Check: The Sheriff shall perform a license check on any dog
found running at large in violation of this article, and if the dog is not
properly licensed in accordance with section
5-2A-2 of this article, the owner shall be issued a citation in accordance with
section
5-2A-9 of this article. Provided however, if the owner obtains a license for
the dog before the appearance date set forth in the citation, and provides
proof of license to the court or prosecutor, the citation shall be dismissed.
   C.   Notice Of Impoundment: If the dog has neither a tag displayed, a
microchip, nor a tattoo number recorded with the City, and the owner thereof is
unknown, or if the owner has been notified, and does not retrieve the dog
within five (5) business days of impoundment, the dog shall be available for
adoption in accordance with the Benewah Humane Society policies and standards.
   D.   Redemption: The owner of any dog impounded by the City and held by the
Benewah Humane Society may reclaim the dog from the Benewah Humane Society
within five (5) business days of impoundment, upon the payment of charges
assessed by Benewah Humane Society, including boarding fees, inoculations,
medicine and veterinarian fees and by providing proof of a City dog license
obtained in accordance with section
5-2A-2 of this article. (Ord. 2019-729, 5-13-2019)
5-2A-7: PUBLIC NUISANCE:
   A.   Public Nuisance Declared: It is hereby declared a public nuisance for
any person owning, harboring, keeping or having in his possession or under his
control a dog, and permitting or allowing such dog to do any of the following:
      1.   To bark, howl or yelp for any consecutive thirty (30) minute period
of time such that it is plainly audible from the public street, alley or
adjacent property.
      2.   To snap, growl, snarl, jump upon or otherwise threaten a person
lawfully using the public sidewalk, streets, alleys, or other public ways.
      3.   To cause injury or to otherwise endanger the safety of persons or
domestic animals, including biting, inflicting injury, assaulting or otherwise
attacking a person or domestic animal unless:
         a.   The dog was protecting or defending a person within the immediate
vicinity of the dog from an attack or assault;
         b.   The person was committing a crime or offense upon the property of
the owner or custodian of the dog;
         c.   The person was at the time, or had in the past, willfully
tormented, abused or assaulted the dog;
         d.   The dog was responding to pain or injury or protecting its
offspring;
         e.   The dog was working as a hunting dog, herding dog or predator
control dog on the property of, or under the control of, its owner or keeper,
and the damage or injury sustained was to a person who was interfering with the
dog while the dog was working in a place where it was lawfully engaged in such
activity, including public lands; or
         f.   The person was intervening between two (2) or more animals
engaged in aggressive behavior or fighting.
      4.   To defecate on public property or on private property not belonging
to the owner of the dog, unless the dog owner immediately removes the waste
material and properly disposes of it.
      5.   To run at large as defined in section
5-2A-5 of this article.
   B.   Notification: Whenever any person shall complain to the Sheriff that a
dog being kept by any person in the City is a public nuisance as declared
herein, the Sheriff shall make reasonable efforts to notify the person(s)
owning, harboring or keeping said dog or dogs that a complaint has been
received and the person should take whatever steps necessary to alleviate the
public nuisance. Failure to abate said nuisance after receiving notice from the
Sheriff shall subject the person(s) owning, harboring or keeping said dog or
dogs to the penalties set forth in section
5-2A-9 of this article. (Ord. 2019-731, 6-24-2019)
5-2A-8: DOGS IN CITY PARKS:
   A.   Leashes Required: It shall be unlawful for any person to take or allow
a dog upon the premises of the City parks unless the dog is on a leash or
confined within a designated dog park/area.
   B.   No Dogs on City beach at Aqua Park: It shall be unlawful for any person
to take or allow a dog whether it is on a leash or not upon the City beach at
Aqua Park.
   C.   Public Events: During events open to the general public at the City
parks it shall be unlawful for any person to take or allow a dog whether it is
on a leash or not upon the premises of the City parks.
   D.   Additional Times: The City Council may specify additional times when it
is unlawful for a person to take or allow a dog whether it is on a leash or not
upon the premises of a particular City park.
   E.   Service Dogs: The prohibitions in this section will not apply to a
service dog as defined by title II and title III of the ADA needed to assist an
individual with a disability or to a dog used by law enforcement in the line of
duty.
   F.   Exemption: Vendors or others with special circumstances may apply to
the City Clerk for an exemption from this section. The exemption may be granted
upon conditions being imposed for the protection of the public. If an exemption
is granted, a certificate shall be given by the City Clerk stating the
exemption and its conditions.
   G.   Posting Of Notice: Whenever dogs are not allowed in a City park for a
particular period, the park shall be conspicuously posted with notices that no
dogs are allowed in the park and that a violation of the prohibition is an
infraction.
   H.   Enforcement: The Sheriff is authorized to enforce this section and to
eject from a City park any person violating this section. (Ord. 2019-729, 5-13-
2019; amd. Ord. 2020-738, 3-23-2020)
5-2A-9: PENALTY:
   A.   Infraction: Any violation of this article, other than subsection
5-2A-7A3 of this article, shall be punishable as follows, notwithstanding that
the dog involved may not be the same dog as was involved in the previous
violation:
      1.   The first violation of this article shall constitute an infraction,
with a set fine of fifty dollars ($50.00) plus court costs.
      2.   The second violation of this article within two (2) years shall
constitute an infraction, with a set fine of one hundred dollars ($100.00) plus
court costs.
      3.   The third or subsequent violation of this article within two (2)
years shall constitute an infraction, punishable fine of double the penalty of
the previous violation, up to a maximum of six hundred dollars ($600.00) plus
court costs.
   B.   Misdemeanor: Any violation of subsection
5-2A-7A3 of this article shall be a misdemeanor and shall be punishable as set
forth in the general penalty in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 2019-731, 6-24-2019)
CHAPTER 3
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
5-3-1: Public Drinking
5-3-1: PUBLIC DRINKING:
   A.   Title: This section shall be known and may be cited as the CITY OF ST.
MARIES PUBLIC DRINKING ORDINANCE.
   B.   Purpose: This section is enacted for the purpose of promoting the
public safety by reducing the hazards incumbent upon the consumption of
alcoholic beverages in public.
   C.   Prohibited Acts:
      1.   Consumption: It is unlawful for any person to consume any beer or
intoxicating liquor, or to have in his possession any opened or open containers
or receptacles containing any beer or intoxicating liquor on any public park,
grounds or thoroughfares within the city or at any other place therein,
including any motor vehicle moving or parked, other than in a private residence
or open premises licensed for the sale and consumption of beer or liquor.
      2.   Possession: It is unlawful for any person to have in his possession
any containers or receptacles containing any beer or intoxicating liquor in any
public park.
   D.   Special Exemptions For Permitted Activities: Upon the issuance of a
permit from the city council for a specially permitted activity, the permit may
exempt the applications of subsection C of this section, either or both,
subject to any terms and conditions of the permit.
   E.   Violation; Penalty: Any person found guilty of violating any provision
of this section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished
as provided in the general penalty in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 632, 8-12-2002)
CHAPTER 4
CURFEW
SECTION:
5-4-1: Title
5-4-2: Purpose
5-4-3: Definitions
5-4-4: Offenses
5-4-5: Defenses
5-4-6: Enforcement
5-4-7: Penalty
5-4-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the ST. MARIES CURFEW
ORDINANCE. (Ord. 599, 8-12-1996)
5-4-2: PURPOSE:
The city council has determined that there has been an increase in juvenile
violence and crimes by persons under the age of eighteen (18) in the city and
persons under the age of eighteen (18) are particularly susceptible, by their
lack of maturity and experience, to participation in unlawful activities and to
be victims of older perpetrators of crime; therefore, the purpose of this
chapter is to provide for the protection of minors from each other and from
other persons, for the enforcement of parental control over and responsibility
for children, for the protection of the general public, and for the reduction
of juvenile criminal activities. (Ord. 599, 8-12-1996)
5-4-3: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
CURFEW HOURS: Eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. every day until six o'clock (6:00)
A.M. of the following day.
EMERGENCY: An unforeseen combination of circumstances or the resulting state
that calls for immediate action. The term includes, but is not limited to, a
fire, a natural disaster, or automobile accident, or any situation requiring
immediate action to prevent serious bodily injury or loss of life.
ESTABLISHMENT: Any privately owned place of business operated for a profit to
which the public is invited, including, but not limited to, any place of
amusement or entertainment.
GUARDIAN: A person who, under court order, is the guardian of the person of a
minor.
MINOR: Any person under eighteen (18) years of age.
OPERATOR: Any individual, firm, association, partnership or corporation
operating, managing or conducting an establishment. This term includes the
members or partners of an association or partnership and the officers of a
corporation.
PARENT: A person who is:
   A.   A natural parent, adoptive parent or stepparent; or
   B.   At least twenty one (21) years of age and specifically authorized in
advance by a parent or guardian to have the care and custody of a minor.
PUBLIC PLACE: Any place to which the public or a substantial group of the
public has access and includes, but is not limited to, streets, highways and
the common areas of schools, hospitals, apartment houses and office buildings.
REMAIN: To:
   A.   Linger or stay; or
   B.   Fail to leave premises when requested to do so by a peace officer or
the owner, operator or other person in control of the premises.
SERIOUS BODILY INJURY: Bodily injury that creates a substantial risk of death
or that causes death, serious permanent disfigurement or protracted loss or
impairment of the function of any bodily member or organ. (Ord. 599, 8-12-1996)
5-4-4: OFFENSES:
   A.   Minor: A minor commits an offense if he remains in any public place or
on the premises of any establishment within the city during curfew hours.
   B.   Parent; Guardian: A parent or guardian of a minor commits an offense if
he knowingly permits, or by insufficient control allows, the minor to remain in
any public place or on the premises of any establishment within the city during
curfew hours.
   C.   Owner, Operator, Employee Of Establishment: The owner, operator or any
employee of an establishment commits an offense if he knowingly allows a minor
to remain upon the premises of the establishment during curfew hours.
   D.   Failure To Take Custody: A parent or guardian commits a separate
offense if he fails to come immediately to a location designated by a police
officer to take custody of a child after being notified to do so by a peace
officer or his designated agent. (Ord. 599, 8-12-1996)
5-4-5: DEFENSES:
   A.   Minor: It is a defense to prosecution under subsection
5-4-4A of this chapter that the minor was:
      1.   Accompanied by the minor's parent or guardian;
      2.   On an errand at the direction of the minor's parent or guardian,
without any detour or stop;
      3.   In a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel;
      4.   Engaged in an employment activity, or going to or returning home
from an employment activity, without any detour or stop;
      5.   Involved in an emergency;
      6.   On the sidewalk abutting the minor's residence;
      7.   Attending an official school, religious or other recreational
activity supervised by adults and sponsored by a government or civic
organization, or other similar entity that takes responsibility for the minor,
or going to or returning home from, without any detour or stop, an official
school, religious or other recreational activity supervised by adults and
sponsored by a government or civic organization, or another similar entity that
takes responsibility for the minor; or
      8.   Exercising first amendment rights protected by the United States
constitution, such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech, and the
right of assembly; or
      9.   Married or had been married.
   B.   Owner, Operator, Employee Of Establishment: It is a defense to
prosecution under subsection
5-4-4C of this chapter that the owner, operator or employee of an establishment
promptly notified the police department that the minor was present on the
premises of the establishment during curfew hours and refused to leave. (Ord.
599, 8-12-1996)
5-4-6: ENFORCEMENT:
Before taking any enforcement action under this chapter, a police officer shall
ask the apparent offender's age and reason for being in the public place. The
officer shall not issue a citation or make an arrest under this chapter unless
the officer reasonably believes that an offense has occurred and that, based on
any response and other circumstances, no defense in section
5-4-5 of this chapter is present. (Ord. 599, 8-12-1996)
5-4-7: PENALTY:
   A.   Adult Violation: A violation of subsections
5-4-4B, C or D of this chapter is a misdemeanor punishable by a fine up to five
hundred dollars ($500.00), or by incarceration up to six (6) months, or both.
   B.   Minor Violation: A violation of subsection
5-4-4A of this chapter may form the basis for a petition or proceedings against
the minor pursuant to the juvenile corrections act 1 . The court may utilize
any of the dispositional alternatives provided by Idaho law for the violation
of a status offense.
   C.   Restitution: The court may order restitution to the city or other
appropriate agencies for any costs reasonably incurred by the city, or other
appropriate agencies, in caring for the child, including, but not limited to,
wages of police officers, law enforcement officials, transportation and
attendant care charges, which resulted from a violation of subsections
5-4-4A, B and C of this chapter. (Ord. 599, 8-12-1996)
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 20-501 et seq.
CHAPTER 5
FAIR HOUSING
SECTION:
5-5-1: Declaration Of Policy
5-5-2: Definitions
5-5-3: Unlawful Practices
5-5-4: Exemptions
5-5-5: Complaint Procedure
5-5-6: Other Remedies
5-5-7: Violation; Penalty
5-5-1: DECLARATION OF POLICY:
It is declared to be the policy of the city, in the exercise of its police
power for the public safety, public health and general welfare, to assure equal
opportunity to all persons to live in decent housing facilities regardless of
race, color, religion, sex or national origin and, to that end, to prohibit
discrimination in housing by any persons. (1977 Code § 9.16.010)
5-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter the following words shall have the following
meanings:
DISCRIMINATION OR DISCRIMINATORY HOUSING PRACTICE: Any difference in treatment
based upon race, color, religion, sex or national origin; or any act that is
unlawful under this chapter.
FINANCIAL INSTITUTION: Includes any person, as defined in this chapter, engaged
in the business of lending money or guaranteeing losses.
HOUSING ACCOMMODATION OR DWELLING: Any building, mobile home or trailer,
structure or portion thereof which is occupied as, or designed, or intended for
occupancy as, a residence by one or more families, and any vacant land which is
offered for sale or lease for the construction or location thereon of any such
building, mobile home or trailer, structure or portion thereof or any real
property, as defined in this chapter, used or intended to be used for any of
the purposes set forth in this chapter.
MORTGAGE BROKER: An individual who is engaged in or who performs the business
or services of a mortgage broker as the same are defined by Idaho statutes.
OPEN MARKET: The market which is informed of the availability for sale,
purchase, rental or lease of any housing accommodation, whether informed
through a real estate broker or by advertising by publication, signs or by any
other advertising methods directed to the public or any portion thereof,
indicating that the property is available for sale, purchase, rental or lease.
OWNER: Includes a lessee, sublessee, cotenant, assignee, managing agent or
other person having the right of ownership or possession, or the right to sell,
rent or lease any housing accommodation.
PERSON: Includes individuals, children, firms, associations, joint ventures,
partnerships, estates, trusts, business trusts, syndicates, fiduciaries,
corporations and all other groups or combinations.
REAL ESTATE BROKER OR REAL ESTATE SALESPERSON: Includes any individual
qualified by law who for a fee, commission, salary or for other valuable
consideration, or who with the intention or expectation of receiving or
collecting the same, lists, sells, purchases, rents or leases any housing
accommodations, including options thereupon, or who negotiates or attempts to
negotiate such activities; or who advertises or holds himself out as engaged in
such activities; or who negotiates or attempts to negotiate a loan, secured by
a mortgage or other encumbrance, upon transfer of any housing accommodation; or
who is engaged in the business of charging an advance fee or contracting for
collection of a fee in connection with a contract whereby he undertakes to
promote the sale, purchase, rental or lease of any housing accommodation
through its listing in a publication issued primarily for such purpose; or any
individual employed by or acting on behalf of any of these.
REAL PROPERTY: Includes buildings, structures, lands, tenements, leaseholds,
cooperatives and condominiums. (1977 Code § 9.16.020)
5-5-3: UNLAWFUL PRACTICES:
In connection with any of the transactions set forth in this section which
affect any housing accommodation on the open market, or in connection with any
public sale, purchase, rental or lease of any housing accommodation, it is
unlawful within the city for a person, owner, financial institution, real
estate broker or real estate salesperson, or any representative of the above,
to:
   A.   Refuse to sell, purchase, rent or lease, or deny to or withhold any
housing accommodation from a person because of his race, color, religion,
ancestry, national origin, sex or place of birth; or
   B.   To discriminate against a person in the terms, conditions or privileges
of the sale, purchase, rental or lease of any housing accommodation, or in the
furnishing of facilities of services in connection therewith; or
   C.   To refuse to receive or transmit a bona fide offer to sell, purchase,
rent or lease any housing accommodation from or to a person because of his
race, color, religion, ancestry, national origin, sex or place of birth; or
   D.   To refuse to negotiate for the sale, purchase, rental or lease of any
housing accommodation to a person because of his race, color, religion,
ancestry, national origin, sex or place of birth; or
   E.   To represent to a person that any housing accommodation is not
available for inspection, sale, purchase, rental or lease when in fact it is so
available, or to refuse to permit a person to inspect any housing
accommodation, because of his race, color, religion or national origin, sex or
place of birth; or
   F.   To make, publish, print, circulate, post or mail, or cause to be made,
published, printed, circulated, posted or mailed, any notice, statement or
advertisement, or to announce a policy, or to sign or to use a form of
application for the sale, purchase, rental, lease or financing of any housing
accommodation, or to make a record of inquiry in connection with the
prospective sale, purchase, rental, lease or financing of any housing
accommodation, or to make a record of inquiry in connection with the
prospective sale, purchase, rental, lease or financing of any housing
accommodation, which indicates any discrimination or any intent to make a
discrimination; or
   G.   To offer, solicit, accept or use a listing of any housing accommodation
for sale, purchase, rental or lease with the understanding that a person may be
subjected to discrimination in connection with such sale, purchase, rental or
lease, or in the furnishing of facilities or services in connection therewith;
or
   H.   To induce directly or indirectly, or attempt to induce directly or
indirectly, the sale, purchase, rental or lease, or the listing for any of the
above, of any housing accommodation by representing that the presence or
anticipated presence of persons of any particular race, color, religion, sex or
national origin or place of birth in the area to be affected by such sale,
purchase, rental or lease will or may result in either:
      1.   The lowering of property values in the area;
      2.   An increase in criminal or antisocial behavior in the area; or
      3.   A decline in the quality of schools serving the area; or
   I.   To make any misrepresentations concerning the listing for sale,
purchase, rental or lease, or the anticipated listing for any of the above, or
the sale, purchase, rental or lease of any housing accommodation in any area in
the city for the purpose of including or attempting to induce any such listing
or any of the above transactions; or
   J.   To engage in, or hire to be done, or to conspire with others to commit
acts or activities of any nature, the purpose of which is to coerce, cause
panic, incite unrest or create or play upon fear, with the purpose of either
discouraging or inducing, or attempting to induce, the sale, purchase, rental
or lease, or the listing for any of the above, of any housing accommodation; or
   K.   To retaliate or discriminate in any manner against a person because he
has opposed a practice declared unlawful by this chapter, or because he has
filed a complaint, testified, assisted or participated in any manner in any
investigation, proceeding, hearing or conference under this chapter; or
   L.   To aid, abet, incite, compel or coerce any person to engage in any of
the practices prohibited by this chapter; or to obstruct or prevent any person
from complying with the provisions of this chapter; or any order issued
thereunder; or
   M.   By canvassing, to commit any unlawful practices prohibited by this
chapter; or
   N.   Otherwise to deny to, or withhold any housing accommodation from a
person because of his race, color, religion, ancestry, national origin, sex or
place of birth; or
   O.   For any bank, building and loan association, insurance company or other
corporation, association, firm or enterprise whose business consists in whole
or in part, in the making of commercial real estate loans, to deny a loan or
other financial assistance to a person applying therefor for the purpose of
purchasing, constructing, improving, repairing or maintaining a dwelling, or to
discriminate against him in the fixing of the amount, interest rate, duration,
or other terms or conditions of such loans or other financial assistance,
because of the race, color, religion, sex or national origin of such person or
of any person associated with him in connection with such loan or other
financial assistance or the purposes of such loan or other financial assistance
or of the present or prospective owners, lessees, tenants or occupants of the
dwelling or dwellings in relation to which such loan or other financial
assistance is to be made or given; or
   P.   To deny any qualified person access to or membership or participation
in any multiple listing service, real estate brokers' organization, or other
service, organization or facility relating to the business of selling or
renting dwellings, or to discriminate against him in their terms or conditions
of such access, membership or participation on account of race, color,
religion, sex or national origin. (1977 Code § 9.16.030)
5-5-4: EXEMPTIONS:
This chapter shall not apply to:
   A.   A religious organization, association or society or any nonprofit
institution or organization operating, supervised or controlled by or in
conjunction with a religious organization, association or society, which limits
the sale, rental or occupancy of dwellings which it owns or operates for other
than commercial purpose to persons of the same religion, or which gives
preference to such persons, unless membership in such a religion is restricted
on account of race, color, sex or national origin;
   B.   A private club not in fact open to the public, which as an incident to
its primary purpose or purposes, provides lodgings which it owns or operates
for other than a commercial purpose, and which limits the rental or occupancy
of such lodgings to its members or gives preference to its members;
   C.   Any single-family house sold or rented by an owner; provided, that such
private individual owner does not own more than three (3) such single-family
houses at any one time; provided further, that in the case of the sale of any
such single-family house by a private individual owner not residing in such
house at the time of such sale or who was not the most recent resident of such
house prior to such sale, the exemption granted by this subsection shall apply
only with respect to one such sale within any twenty four (24) month period;
provided further, that such bona fide private individual owner does not own any
interest in, nor is there owned or served on his behalf, under any express or
voluntary agreement, title to or any right to all or a portion of the proceeds
from the sale or rental of more than three (3) such single-family houses at any
one time; provided further, the sale or rental of any such single-family house
shall be excepted from the application of this chapter only if such house is
sold or rented:
      1.   Without the use in any manner of the sales or rental facilities or
the sales or rental services of any real estate broker, agent or salesperson,
or of such facilities or services of any person in the business of selling or
renting dwellings, or of any employee or agent of any such broker, agent,
salesperson or person; and
      2.   Without the publication, posting or mailing, after notice, of any
advertisement or written notice in violation of the provisions of 42 United
States Code section 3604(c) or of section
5-5-3 of this chapter; but nothing in this section shall prohibit the use of
attorneys, escrow agents, abstractors, title companies and other such
professional assistance as necessary to perfect or transfer the title; or
   D.   Rooms or units in dwellings containing living quarters occupied or
intended to be occupied by no more than four (4) families living independently
of each other, if the owner actually maintains and occupies one of such living
quarters as his residence. (1977 Code § 9.16.040)
5-5-5: COMPLAINT PROCEDURE:
Any person aggrieved by an unlawful practice prohibited by this chapter may
file a complaint with the city attorney within thirty (30) days after the
aggrieved person becomes aware of the alleged unlawful practice, and in no
event more than sixty (60) days after the alleged unlawful practice occurred.
The city attorney or his duly authorized representative shall investigate each
complaint and attempt to resolve each complaint. Failure to achieve a
resolution acceptable to both parties and compliance with this chapter shall
cause the city attorney to forward the complaint and his findings to
appropriate state and federal officials. (1977 Code § 9.16.050)
5-5-6: OTHER REMEDIES:
Nothing contained in this chapter shall prevent any person from exercising any
right or seeking any remedy to which he might otherwise be entitled or from
filing his complaint with any appropriate governmental agency. (1977 Code §
9.16.060)
5-5-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall, upon conviction
thereof, be punished as provided by law. (1977 Code § 9.16.070)
CHAPTER 6
ABANDONED, WRECKED, DISMANTLED AND INOPERATIVE MOTOR VEHICLES
SECTION:
5-6-1: Title
5-6-2: Definitions
5-6-3: Storing, Parking Or Leaving Prohibited
5-6-4: Notice To Remove
5-6-5: Responsibility For Removal
5-6-6: Notice Of Procedure
5-6-7: Redemption Of Impounded Vehicles
5-6-8: Immunity From Damages
5-6-9: Violation; Penalty
5-6-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the ABANDONED, WRECKED,
DISMANTLED AND INOPERATIVE VEHICLE ORDINANCE of the City. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-
2018)
5-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms, phrases, words and their
derivations shall have the meaning given herein. When not inconsistent with the
context, words used in the present tense include the future, words in the
plural number include the singular number, and words in the singular number
include the plural number. The word "shall" is always mandatory and not merely
directory.
CITY: The City of St. Maries, Benewah County, Idaho.
JUNKED VEHICLE: Any "vehicle", as defined herein, which does not have lawfully
affixed thereto both an unexpired license plate or plates or a current
registration certificate if such is required by law and the condition of which
is wrecked, dismantled, partially dismantled, inoperative, abandoned or
discarded.
PERSON: Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or
organization of any kind.
PUBLIC PROPERTY: Any public street, alley or highway which shall include the
entire width between the boundary lines of every way publicly maintained for
the purposes of vehicular travel and shall also mean any other City owned
property or facility.
VEHICLE: Every device in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be
transported or drawn upon a street, highway or waterway, excepting devices used
exclusively upon stationary rails and tracks, and shall include, but not be
limited to, automobiles, buses, motorbikes, ATVs, motorcycles, motorscooters,
trucks, tractors, go-carts, golf carts, campers, trailers and boats. (Ord.
2018-723, 7-23-2018)
5-6-3: STORING, PARKING OR LEAVING PROHIBITED:
No person shall park, store, leave or permit the parking, storing or leaving of
any vehicle of any kind which is abandoned, wrecked, dismantled, inoperative,
rusted, junked or partially dismantled, whether attended or not, upon any
public property of the City for any period of time in excess of seventy two
(72) hours. The presence of an abandoned, wrecked, dismantled, inoperative,
rusted, junked or partially dismantled vehicle or parts thereof on public
property is hereby declared a public nuisance which may be abated in accordance
with the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
5-6-4: NOTICE TO REMOVE:
Whenever it comes to the attention of any City police officer or the Benewah
County Sheriff or one of his duly constituted deputies and/or any authorized
City employee, that any nuisance as defined in section
5-6-3 of this chapter exists in the City, a notice, in writing, shall be served
upon the owner of the vehicle, if known, and a notice to remove shall be placed
in a conspicuous place on the vehicle requesting its removal in the time
specified in this chapter. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
5-6-5: RESPONSIBILITY FOR REMOVAL:
Upon proper notice and opportunity to be heard, the owner of the abandoned,
wrecked, dismantled or inoperative vehicle shall be responsible for its
removal. In the event of removal and disposition by the City, the owner of the
vehicle shall be liable for the expenses incurred. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
5-6-6: NOTICE OF PROCEDURE:
   A.   Notice Required: Any City police officer or the Benewah County Sheriff
or one of his duly constituted deputies and/or any authorized City employee,
shall give notice of removal to the owner of the vehicle, if known, at least
three (3) days before the time of compliance. It shall constitute sufficient
notice when a copy of the same is posted in a conspicuous place upon the
vehicle and duplicate copies are sent by certified or registered mail to the
owner of the vehicle, if known, at his last known address.
   B.   Content Of Notice: Notice shall contain the request for removal within
the time specified in this chapter, and the notice shall advise that upon
failure to comply with the notice to remove, the City, or its designee, shall
undertake such removal with costs to be levied against the owner of the
vehicle. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
5-6-7: REDEMPTION OF IMPOUNDED VEHICLES:
The owner of any vehicle seized under the provisions of this chapter may redeem
such vehicle at any time after its removal but prior to sale or destruction
thereof on proof of ownership and payment to the business establishment where
the vehicle is impounded. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
5-6-8: IMMUNITY FROM DAMAGES:
Any police officer, towing service owner, operator or employee shall not be
held to answer or be liable for damages in any action brought by the registered
owner or his legal representative or any person legally entitled to the
possession of a motor vehicle or other vehicle when the vehicle was processed
and sold or disposed of as provided by this chapter. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
5-6-9: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person violating any provisions of this chapter shall be guilty of an
infraction and upon conviction, shall be subject to a fine as provided in the
general penalty in section
1-4-1 of this Code. Each act in violation of any of the provisions thereof
shall be deemed a separate offense. (Ord. 2018-723, 7-23-2018)
TITLE 6
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL TRAFFIC PROVISIONS
SECTION:
6-1-1: Local Control
6-1-2: Obedience Required
6-1-3: One Way Streets
6-1-4: Violation; Penalty
6-1-1: LOCAL CONTROL:
   A.   Authority: In all matters relating to traffic control not covered in
the stipulations of this title, the public works directors shall have full
power to make necessary regulations governing the same. In all points of
dispute as to the interpretation of the stipulations of this title, the public
works directors' decision shall be final and binding on all parties. (1977 Code
§ 10.04.040)
   B.   Signs: The public works directors, under the direction of the city
council, shall have power to erect or cause to be erected proper signs or
signals on any street or street intersection or at an railroad crossing
directing the method and tim of parking, the character of vehicles allowed to
park or stop and directing that vehicles shall stop or slow down at designated
points; or notifying the public of the location of schools and hospitals and
dangerous street intersections or crossing or of any other conditions affecting
the traffic and control of same. (1977 Code § 10.04.010)
6-1-2: OBEDIENCE REQUIRED:
All persons driving or operating vehicles, riding horseback or walking on the
streets and alleys shall at all times obey the orders, direction and signals of
all police officers directing traffic. (1977 Code § 10.04.030)
6-1-3: ONE WAY STREETS:
   A.   Designation Of One Way Streets: The city, acting though its city
council or the public works directors, may designate any street or roadway
under its jurisdiction for one way traffic, and shall cause to be erected
appropriate signs at intersections giving notice thereof. (1977 Code §
10.04.050)
   B.   Signs: Upon a street or roadway designated and signposted for one way
traffic, a vehicle shall be driven only in the direction designated. (1977 Code
§ 10.04.060)
   C.   Validation: Any streets or roadways designated one way streets before
the effective date hereof within the purview of this section, are validated and
declared to be one any streets. (1977 Code § 10.04.070)
6-1-4: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person who disregards, disobeys or fails to observe any traffic sign or
signs regulating traffic within the city, such as stop signs, signs limiting
parking of motor vehicles or any other traffic signs placed in the city by
order of the mayor and city council or public works directors, shall be deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished as
provided in the general penalty in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1977 Code § 10.04.080)
CHAPTER 2
PARKING REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-2-1: Title
6-2-2: Purpose
6-2-3: Definitions
6-2-4: Parking Areas Designated
6-2-5: Parking Restrictions
6-2-6: Nuisance Declared
6-2-7: Unlawfully Parked Vehicles; Impoundment
6-2-8: Violation; Penalty
6-2-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the CITY OF ST. MARIES PARKING
ORDINANCE. (1977 Code § 10.08.010)
6-2-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to ensure the rights of way and other public
properties are utilized in a manner consistent with the health, safety and
welfare of the citizens of the city and consistent with the city's
responsibility and its proprietary interest in the public rights of way of the
city and other public properties. (1977 Code § 10.08.020)
6-2-3: DEFINITIONS:
All terms used in this chapter shall have the meaning given to them by Idaho
Code. (1977 Code § 10.08.030)
6-2-4: PARKING AREAS DESIGNATED:
The public works directors, with city council approval, are authorized:
   A.   Designation Of Parking Areas: To designate such parking areas as are
necessary for the purposes of limited parking for, but not limited to, the
following purposes: handicapped parking, loading zones, bus stop zones, taxi
zones, parking relating to emergency or medical services, permit parking areas
where the stopping or parking of vehicles would create hazardous conditions or
cause unusual delay in traffic.
   B.   Prohibit Parking: To prohibit parking on narrow streets.
   C.   Erect Signs: To erect such signs as are necessary to provide notice to
the driving public of such zones.
   D.   Painting Of Curbs: To cause curbs to be painted to provide notice that
the space or area adjacent to the curb is a no parking area. Parking adjacent
to a curb which is painted yellow or red shall constitute a violation of this
chapter. This section shall be applicable to private property as well as public
property. (1977 Code § 10.08.060)
6-2-5: PARKING RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Limited Parking: Where, in the public interest, the city council
determines that various parking areas on public rights of way or property
should have limited time duration parking or have restricted hours on parking,
the city council, may, by resolution, regulate and restrict public parking in
such manner as it determines to be in the public interest. (1977 Code §
10.08.050; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Handicapped Parking: It is unlawful for any person to stop, stand or
park a vehicle in a designated handicapped parking space or area as defined in
Idaho Code 49-213, unless the occupant has complied with Idaho Code 49-410.
This section shall apply to both public and private parking areas which are
properly designated. (1977 Code § 10.08.120)
   C.   Prohibited Parking:
      1.   Fire Lanes: It is in violation of this chapter for any vehicle to
park in a fire lane, either on public or private property. (1977 Code §
10.08.150)
      2.   Alleys: It shall be a violation of this chapter for any person to
park a vehicle within any alley of the city. However, it shall be lawful for a
vehicle to remain stationary within an alley for the minimum period of time
necessary to load or unload such vehicle, if the only reasonable location from
which said vehicle may be loaded or unloaded would be such alley. (1977 Code §
10.08.100)
      3.   Repairing Vehicles: No construction, repairing, overhauling,
remodeling or other type of work other than in case of extreme emergency shall
be performed on any vehicle or other property upon any street, alley, park,
parking lot or other public property within the city. (1977 Code § 10.08.110)
      4.   Loading And Unloading: Loading and unloading of vehicles shall only
take place in specified loading zones. (1977 Code § 10.08.080; amd. 2004 Code)
      5.   General Prohibition: It is unlawful for any person to stop, stand or
park a vehicle, except when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic or
in compliance with law or the direction of a police officer or traffic control
device in any of the following places:
         a.   In any place where prohibited by Idaho Code 49-660.
         b.   In any place where signs have been erected at the direction of
the public works directors or city council. (1977 Code § 10.08.090)
6-2-6: NUISANCE DECLARED:
   A.   Declared Nuisance: Any vehicle parked in violation of the provisions of
this chapter is declared to be a nuisance. It is further declared that any
vehicle parking on city property, including public rights of way, in violation
of this section shall be considered to be trespassing on public property. It is
further declared that the registered owner of the vehicle shall be deemed the
party responsible for the unlawful use of such vehicle as to the provisions of
this chapter and shall be prima facie responsible for any violation as to the
unattended standing or parking of his vehicle.
   B.   Exceptions: Any charge under this chapter shall be dismissed when the
person charged has made a bona fide sale or transfer of the vehicle and has
delivered possession thereof through the purchaser, and has advised the police
department, within twenty (20) days of notice of the violation, of the name and
address of the purchaser along with proof of the date of sale. (1977 Code §
10.08.040)
6-2-7: UNLAWFULLY PARKED VEHICLES; IMPOUNDMENT:
The chief of police, or his authorized designee, may remove and impound any
unlawfully parked vehicle or cause the registered owner to be issued with a
citation, or both. In addition to any fines or fees that such unlawfully parked
vehicles may be subject to under this chapter, the registered owner shall be
liable to the city for all costs and expenses incurred in the removal,
impounding and storage of such unlawfully parked vehicle. (1977 Code §
10.08.130)
6-2-8: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
   A.   Infraction: Any violation of any provision of this chapter shall be
considered an infraction, punishable in accordance with subsection
1-4-1B of this code.
   B.   Separate Violation: Each limited time period for which a vehicle is
parked shall constitute a separate violation of this chapter (if a vehicle is
parked more than 3 hours in a 90 minute limited parking zone, 2 separate
violations have taken place). Either the registered owner of the vehicle or the
driver, if known, may be cited. However, only one citation may issue for each
violation. (1977 Code § 10.08.160)
   C.   Penalty: The penalty for such an infraction is twenty five dollars
($25.00), except for parking in a handicap zone or next to a fire hydrant that
shall be one hundred dollars ($100.00). The citation shall be paid to the City
Clerk of St. Maries within ten (10) days of the violation. Failure or refusal
to pay the fine set forth on the parking citation shall result in further
action being taken by the city, including, but not limited to, initiating
collection procedures via a debt collection service, filing a civil lawsuit for
collection of the unpaid penalty(ies), and subject to subsection E of this
section, filing a misdemeanor complaint. Provided, further, the city shall be
entitled to all fees, costs, and attorney fees incurred in the collection of
such fees, and, upon entry of judgment, the city shall have each, every, and
all rights of enforcement of a judgment as provided by the Idaho Code. (1977
Code § 10.08.140)
   D.   Parking Policy: The St. Maries City Council has promulgated its Parking
Regulations that govern parking policies within the City, which may be amended
from time to time by further Resolution of the City Council.
   E.   Misdemeanor: The failure to pay four (4) or more civil penalties
assessed for a parking violation shall constitute a misdemeanor and punishable
as set forth in section
1-4-1A of this Code. (amd. Ord. 2023-767, 3- -2023)
CHAPTER 3
MOTOR VEHICLES IN CITY PARKS
SECTION:
6-3-1: Title
6-3-2: Parking Or Use Prohibited
6-3-3: Signs
6-3-4: Vehicle Removal; Impoundment
6-3-5: Exceptions
6-3-6: Permits
6-3-7: Violation; Penalty
6-3-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and be cited as the ST. MARIES CITY PARKS PARKING
AND OPERATING OF VEHICLES PROHIBITION ORDINANCE. (1977 Code § 10.10.010)
6-3-2: PARKING OR USE PROHIBITED:
Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, no person shall park or operate
any vehicle within the confines of a city park of the city. (1977 Code §
10.10.020)
6-3-3: SIGNS:
The city shall cause to be erected signs at the entry way to all city parks,
said signs clearly designating the city park as a no parking or operating of
vehicles area. The signs so erected shall be in accordance with all state
requirements for traffic control signs. (1977 Code § 10.10.030)
6-3-4: VEHICLE REMOVAL; IMPOUNDMENT:
   A.   Removal: The police department, and all members thereof assigned to
traffic duty, are authorized to have removed and towed away by commercial
towing service, any car or other vehicle illegally parked within any one of the
city parks of the city.
   B.   Impoundment: Cars towed away for illegal parking shall be stored at
owner's risk and expense and shall be restored to the owner or operator of such
car upon payment of the commercial towing fee and the accrued storage thereon.
   C.   Unredeemed Vehicles: Any vehicle not claimed within thirty (30) days
shall be deemed to have been abandoned and thereafter processed pursuant to
