Idaho laws governing abandoned vehicles 1 . (1977 Code § 10.10.040)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 5, chapter 6 of this code.
6-3-5: EXCEPTIONS:
Vehicles owned or operated by the city and used for authorized city purposes,
emergency vehicles, garbage collection vehicles being utilized in collecting
park garbage and refuse and vehicles operated by state, county and city law
enforcement officers while engaged in their official duties are exempt from the
provisions of this chapter. Areas designated by the city for parking or
operation of vehicles and so posted are also excepted. (1977 Code § 10.10.050)
6-3-6: PERMITS:
Persons or organizations having a legitimate need for parking and operating
vehicles within the confines of the city parks may apply to the city clerk for
a permit authorizing the operating and/or parking of vehicles within the
confines of the city parks. The city clerk is authorized to issue permits on an
event only basis. Any permit issued for other than an event basis must be
approved by the mayor or the city council. Permits issued pursuant to this
section will be at the sole discretion of the city. Any request for permits
denied by the city clerk or the mayor may be appealed to the city council for
reconsideration. (1977 Code § 10.10.060)
6-3-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person parking or operating a vehicle in a city park in violation of this
chapter shall be guilty of an infraction and upon being found to have committed
an infraction shall be punished as provided in subsection
1-4-1B of this code. (1977 Code § 10.10.070)
TITLE 7
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
STREETS AND PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
7-1-1: Supervision And Control
7-1-2: City Base And Street Grades Established
7-1-3: Design Standards And Specifications
7-1-4: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
7-1-5: Overhanging Trees And Shrubbery
7-1-6: Winter Street Policy
7-1-7: Violation; Penalty
7-1-1: SUPERVISION AND CONTROL:
   A.   Public Works Directors: All streets, alleys and public thoroughfares in
the city shall be under the immediate supervision and control of the public
works directors, subject to the orders of the mayor and the city council. (1977
Code § 12.04.010)
   B.   Building Inspector: The building inspector shall be charged with
supervision of the construction of any and all streets. Upon satisfaction of
the building inspector, based upon actual inspection and final approval by the
public works directors that construction is in compliance with all codes and
requirements, certificates of compliance shall be issued. Such certificate
shall be a copy of the signed and dated inspection record as made by the public
works directors and shall be issued prior to use. (1977 Code § 12.04.016)
7-1-2: CITY BASE AND STREET GRADES ESTABLISHED:
   A.   Baseline: A city base is fixed and established at a point at the
northwest corner of the intersection of First Street and College Avenue, the
said point being two thousand one hundred forty eight and thirty one-hundredths
feet (2,148.30') above sea level and marked by an iron bar. All official grades
and elevations fixed and established on any of the streets and avenues and
sidewalks of the city shall be with reference to and computed from the city
base as fixed and established in this section. (1977 Code § 12.04.130)
   B.   Street Grades: All grades and lines shall be established and approved
by the public works directors in accordance with ordinances establishing the
grade lines of the various streets and curbs. (1977 Code § 12.04.140)
7-1-3: DESIGN STANDARDS AND SPECIFICATIONS 1 :
Design standards and specifications, for all streets, sidewalks, other public
ways and all right of way encroachments within the city, together with all work
and work procedures done thereon, shall be those current standards and
specifications on file with the city, and by this reference, made a part of
this chapter. (2004 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See section 11-12-1 of this code for fees.
7-1-4: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   Heavy Materials Or Vehicles: It is hereby unlawful for any person to:
      1.   Drag, push, pull or otherwise propel any poles, logs, ties, boards,
or other pieces of timber, or heavy material, over any grades or otherwise
improved streets within the city. (1977 Code § 12.04.030)
      2.   Drive, drag, pull, push or otherwise propel over or upon any graded
or otherwise improved street within the city; or cause to be driven, dragged,
pulled, pushed or propelled over the improved streets of the city, any drag
rack, logging dray, or other heavy vehicle or machine or thing which will be
destructive or tend to interfere with or injure the surface, base, or any part
of such street or avenue of the city. (1977 Code § 12.04.040)
   B.   Propelling Vehicle Over Curb: It is unlawful for any person to back,
push, or otherwise propel any auto, truck, wagon or any vehicle of any nature
whatsoever over or across any curb on any of the streets and avenues of the
city, or cause the same to be done, other than in a place specially provided
for each purpose and, if so provided, it must be done pursuant to the rules and
approval of the public works directors. (1977 Code § 12.04.050)
   C.   Coasting And Sleigh Riding: It is unlawful for any person to coast or
slide with a sled, scooter, wagon, or any other vehicle or instrument or
appliance upon any street or sidewalk within the city except that during the
sleighing season certain streets and avenues of the city may be set apart and
designated for the purpose of coasting and sleighing under such rules and
regulations as shall be adopted by the city council. (1977 Code § 12.04.060)
   D.   Driving On Sidewalks: It is unlawful for any person to drive or cause
to be driven any wagon, automobile, truck or any other vehicle of any kind or
nature across any of the sidewalks of the city other than at a place specially
constructed for such purpose. (1977 Code § 12.12.130)
   E.   Obstructions:
      1.   Gutters And Pipes: It is unlawful for any person to obstruct any of
the gutters on any street within the city, or to obstruct any artificial
carrier or conductor of any surface waters or to, in any manner, obstruct any
pipe, drain, sewer or other carrier or conductor of surface waters or sewerage
whether above or underneath any street or property within the city by placing
thereon or therein any dirt, refuse, snow, ice or any other matter or thing
which shall in any manner prevent the free discharge and drainage of water
through, over or in such gutters, pipes or other carriers or drains. (1977 Code
§ 12.04.070)
      2.   Streets: It is unlawful for any person to in any manner obstruct any
of the streets, or avenues within the city, by placing or leaving thereon any
brick, rock or any other material which will have a tendency to obstruct or
blockade the free use of such streets or avenues; provided, however, that
nothing herein contained shall prevent the city council or the public works
committee of the city from authorizing the use of such portions of any street
or avenue as may be necessary for the piling of lumber and building material to
be used in the actual construction of buildings, or in the repair or alteration
of existing buildings. (1977 Code § 12.04.080; amd. Ord. 2014-692, 2-10-2014)
7-1-5: OVERHANGING TREES AND SHRUBBERY:
All shade trees, including fruit bearing trees, located within the boundaries
of a dedicated street or alley shall have all foliage, including leaves and
branches, trimmed up to a point eight feet (8') above the level of the sidewalk
under or near said trees, and if there is no sidewalk, to a point eight and
one-half feet (8.5') above the average level of the traveled roadway opposite
said trees. (1977 Code § 10.04.020)
7-1-6: WINTER STREET POLICY:
   A.   Parking: It shall be illegal for any vehicle to be parked in such a
manner so as to impede snow removal operations. Any vehicle left in the street
or right of way may be subject to citation and/or removal, at the owner's
expense. Owners may return vehicles to "on street" parking following the
completion of the plowing operations.
Vehicles left in the right of way are left there at the owner's risk and could
be struck by a snowplow during plowing operations. In the event there is damage
to a snowplow or other city equipment caused by vehicles left in the right of
way, owners of said vehicle could be subject to reimbursing the city the cost
of the damage. The city is not liable for damage to any privately owned
vehicles, boats, trailers, etc., when parked in the city right of way.
   B.   Right Of Way Encroachments: Mailboxes, newspaper boxes, fences, and
other personal property located in the street right of way are the
responsibility of the owner. Damage to personal property located in the city
right of way resulting from plowing operations is not a reimbursable expense.
Owners of personal property located in the city right of way could be subject
to reimbursing the city should damage occur to city equipment during plowing
operations.
   C.   Accumulations From Private Property: It is unlawful for any person to
deposit or cause to be deposited, throw upon, or move onto any public street,
sidewalk, thoroughfare or other public property including right of way, any
snow, ice, dirt, soil, rock, or debris that has accumulated on any private
property.
   D.   Sidewalks: Owners and occupants of privately owned premises shall be
responsible for keeping their sidewalks and any areas adjacent to their
business or premises or any portion of their real property, including corners,
free and clear of snow and ice.
   E.   Penalty: Violation of this section or any part thereof shall be a
misdemeanor subject to punishment to the maximum allowed by Idaho Code. (Ord.
660, 12-10-2007)
7-1-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person who violates or fails to comply with any of the provisions of this
chapter or who, having obtained a permit hereunder, wilfully fails to comply
with the conditions herein set forth, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor
and upon conviction thereof shall be fined as provided in the general penalty
in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each successive act constitutes a new violation. (1977 Code
§§ 12.04.018A, 12.04.150; amd. Ord. 660, 12-10-2007)
CHAPTER 2
CEMETERY REGULATIONS
SECTION:
7-2-1: Cemetery Lots, Sales And Regulations
7-2-2: Permit Required
7-2-3: Rates And Charges
7-2-4: Design Standards
7-2-5: General Regulations And Restrictions
7-2-6: Prohibited Acts
7-2-7: Violation; Penalty
7-2-8: Perpetual Care Cemetery Fund; Endowment Care Funds
7-2-9: Burial Of Veterans
7-2-1: CEMETERY LOTS, SALES AND REGULATIONS:
   A.   All lots and parcels of ground in Woodlawn Cemetery which the City
shall sell will be conveyed by certificate, giving the owner the right of
possession forever, as a place of interment of the dead; subject, however, to
such rules of the Woodlawn Cemetery as shall be in force at the time of the
purchase, or that may be adopted thereafter for the general good of the
cemetery. Transfer or sale of ownership of lots must be completed by
"quitclaim" deed and filed at City Hall. If ownership is transferred by
inheritance, such documents must be filed at City Hall. A transfer fee shall be
paid as set by resolution of the City Council for each transfer of a lot.
   B.   All lots shall be sold and/or reserved on a next available space in the
desired block or row. The purpose of this requirement is to keep uniformity in
the cemetery and maintenance expenses down. Graves are available for purchase
at time of need or reserved by purchase prior to need going from east to west.
   C.   Lots in the designated veterans' section may not be reserved except as
may be allowed by resolution of the City Council.
   D.   A maximum of three (3) urns and one body may be placed on a single lot.
If a full body burial does not exist, a maximum of four (4) urns may be placed
on a single lot. (Ord. 2018-722, 6-11-2018)
7-2-2: PERMIT REQUIRED:
When a body is to be removed from one part of the cemetery to another part of
the cemetery, or to another place of interment, a permit issued by the
Department of Health and Welfare must be obtained prior to the removal of the
body. The removal must be witnessed by a licensed funeral director. (Ord. 2018-
722, 6-11-2018)
7-2-3: RATES AND CHARGES:
   A.   The fees charged to purchase cemetery spaces and columbarium niches,
and the fees charged for opening and closing of the space or columbarium, and
the fee charged for perpetual care will be as stated in the current cemetery
fee schedule, as set forth in that certain amending ordinance 635, as adopted
on January 27, 2003, until such time as the fee schedule may be changed by
resolution at any time deemed necessary by the City Council.
   B.   Lots in any area of the cemetery, including the veterans' section are
at no cost to veterans who have been residents of Benewah County for five (5)
or more consecutive years at any time during their lifetime. Perpetual care and
opening and closing fees must still be paid. Lots for the veteran's spouse are
to be paid in accordance to the fee set by City Council. (Ord. 2018-722, 6-11-
2018)
7-2-4: DESIGN STANDARDS:
   A.   Monuments And Headstones: No monument or headstone shall be placed in
any lot without permission of the Superintendent and it shall be his/her duty
to direct and supervise the location and placement of the same, and no monument
or headstone shall be so placed as to interfere with any important effects upon
adjoining lots. The cement foundation of all monuments and headstones shall not
be less than four inches (4") thick, and a minimum of six inches (6") of cement
must border the headstone with the cement base being laid flush with ground
level. The first monument or headstone placed on lot is not required to be
flush with the ground. Any additional monuments or headstones placed on the
same lot must be flush to the ground.
   B.   Fences, Railings And Ornamentation:
      1.   Fences And Railings Prohibited: No lot or parcel of ground shall be
surrounded by any so called fence, railing, embankment or ditch.
      2.   Ornamental Objects: No lot shall contain any glass objects, seat, or
metal or rock works, or any other ornamental objects, except by written
permission of the Superintendent. No ornamentation, decorating monuments or
headstones may be wider than the headstone. The cement foundation of the
monument or headstone must be at least four inches (4") thick and extend a
minimum of six inches (6") from the ornamentation and must be laid at ground
level. No ornamentation may extend higher than thirty six inches (36") from the
ground.
      3.   Trees And Shrubs: No lot shall be decorated by its owner or other
parties interested therein with any tree or shrub without the written
permission of the Superintendent. The Superintendent shall, under the direction
of the City Council, have entire charge of the plantings of trees and shrubs,
in accordance with the general plan, for the ornamentation of the grounds. If
any trees and shrubs shall become, by means of its roots, branches, or
otherwise, detrimental to adjacent lots or avenues, or for any reason its
removal shall become necessary or advisable, the Superintendent shall have the
right, and it shall be his/her duty, to remove such trees or shrubs or any part
thereof.
   C.   Memory Wall Space: All engravings to be placed on the memory wall space
shall measure three inches by nineteen inches (3" x 19"). The engravings shall
contain the deceased person's name, year of birth, and year of death and shall
be engraved using size three-fourths inch (3/4") in font roman lettering. (Ord.
2018-722, 6-11-2018)
7-2-5: GENERAL REGULATIONS AND RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Funeral Hours Permitted: Funerals shall, unless special permission be
granted by the Superintendent, take place between the hours of nine o'clock (9:
00) A.M. and four o'clock (4:00) P.M.
   B.   Driving Restrictions: Fast driving and driving off the pavement are
strictly prohibited.
   C.   Workers: In every case where non-City employee workmen are employed by
owners of lots to do work or make improvements in or about said lots, such
workmen shall be subject to the control and direction of the Superintendent;
and any workman who shall neglect or refuse to obey said direction, or who
shall carelessly or wilfully do injury to adjacent lots, or who shall neglect
to remove any rubbish accumulated in his work, will not thereafter be permitted
to work in the grounds of the cemetery.
   D.   Removal Of Undesirable Persons: The Superintendent and cemetery
employees are instructed to prevent the entrance of all improper persons, and
also all those who may be known to have at any time wilfully transgressed the
rules of the cemetery. It is also the Superintendent's duty to remove from the
grounds all who violate any of the rules, or commit any trespass or
depredation. (Ord. 2018-722, 6-11-2018)
7-2-6: PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   Picnics: Picnics, parties, or persons with refreshments or liquors will
not be admitted on the grounds.
   B.   Firearms And Dogs: No person with firearms will be permitted on the
grounds of the cemetery, with the exception of military salutes. Dogs must be
confined to the vehicle at all times.
   C.   Disturbing Behavior: Boisterous and profane language, and any conduct
tending to disturb the quiet and good order of the cemetery, are forbidden.
   D.   Picking Flowers; Defacing Property: Visitors and all persons who shall
enter the grounds are forbidden to break or injure any tree or shrub, pick
flowers, or to write upon, deface, or desecrate any wall, monument, or
gravestone.
   E.   Tipping Attendants: No money shall be paid to the attendants at the
entrance or on the grounds. (Ord. 2018-722, 6-11-2018)
7-2-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation who shall violate any of the provisions of this
chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be
punished as set forth in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-722, 6-11-
2018)
7-2-8: PERPETUAL CARE CEMETERY FUND; ENDOWMENT CARE FUNDS:
A perpetual care fee shall be charged in accordance with any current cemetery
fee schedule then in effect, for the purpose of maintaining a permanent,
Perpetual Care Reserve Fund of not less than fifty thousand dollars
($50,000.00), from which only the interest earned may be used for cemetery
maintenance and operations. In addition to said reserve fund, all perpetual
care fees or interest earned on the reserve fund shall be deposited to the
Woodlawn Cemetery account or accounts and shall be segregated from the general
funds of the City of St. Maries at the end of each quarter into such account or
accounts, and shall be used solely for expenditures and capital improvements to
Woodlawn Cemetery, City of St. Maries. Any endowment funds received from any
source, such as an estate, a testamentary bequest, a trust distribution, a
charitable donation or gift that are specifically designated to be used for a
special purpose shall be segregated from other cemetery funds and shall be used
solely for the purpose so designated. (Ord. 2018-722, 6-11-2018)
7-2-9: BURIAL OF VETERANS:
   A.   The City Council may by resolution designate a section or sections in
the cemetery for burial of veterans. The remains of the veteran's spouse may be
placed in the same lot as the veteran or in an adjacent lot at the time of
need. If the remains of the veteran's spouse are placed in the veterans'
section before the remains of the veteran, the veteran must agree in writing
(with a contract with the City or a prepaid funeral plan with a funeral home
indicating interment wishes) at that time to have his remains placed in the
same lot, or in a lot adjacent to the remains of the spouse.
   B.   Lots in the veterans' section may not be reserved except as may be
allowed by resolution of the City Council. Veterans may reserve a lot in any
area of the cemetery except in a designated veterans' section. Blocks 141 to
143 rows A and B are to be used by a veteran receiving, at the time of the
veteran's death or veteran's spouse, one single lot. There will be no adjacent
spaces for the veteran's spouse who desires burial. One body and one urn or up
to three (3) urns may be placed in a single veteran's lot. Block 144 is
reserved for only veterans and adjacent spaces for spouse at time of need where
cremation is undesirable to the veteran and the veteran's spouse for whatever
reason including religious or personal concerns. (Ord. 2018-722, 6-11-2018)
CHAPTER 3
TREES AND SHRUBS
SECTION:
7-3-1: Title
7-3-2: Purpose
7-3-3: Definitions
7-3-4: Tree Committee
7-3-5: Authority And Control Over Trees
7-3-6: Removal Of Public Trees And Shrubs
7-3-7: Planting Of Public Trees And Shrubs
7-3-8: Permit Required
7-3-9: Damaging, Destroying Or Topping Of Public Trees Or Shrubs
7-3-10: Care Of Trees Within The City
7-3-11: Penalty
7-3-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be titled as the ST. MARIES TREE ORDINANCE.
(Ord. 650-1, 3-13-2006)
7-3-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to protect trees and shrubs planted and growing
within the public rights of ways, city parks, and within or on all other
property owned or otherwise under the control of the city; to establish and
maintain species variety and age diversity of trees on public lands in the
city; to maintain city trees in a healthy and nonhazardous condition through
standard arboricultural practices. (Ord. 650-1, 3-13-2006)
7-3-3: DEFINITIONS:
DAMAGES: Injury or harm that impairs the health, vigor, value, or usefulness of
a tree, as determined by the St. Maries tree committee.
PARK TREE: Any tree within the boundaries of a designated city park.
PARKWAY: That portion of a street between a roadway and sidewalk.
PUBLIC PROPERTY: Property owned by the city of St. Maries either in fee simple
absolute, or implied, or expressly dedicated to the public for present or
future use for purposes of vehicular or pedestrian traffic, or for public
easements.
PUBLIC TREE OR SHRUB: Any tree or shrub that is situated in such a manner that
fifty one percent (51%) or more of the tree trunk or shrub base at ground level
is on public property or public right of way.
SIDEWALK: That portion of a street between the curb lines, or the lateral lines
of a roadway, and the adjacent property lines intended for the use of
pedestrians.
STREET: The entire width between the boundary lines of a public right of way
dedicated or deeded to the city for use of the public for purposes of vehicular
travel, whether or not maintained by the city and whether or not open for
vehicular traffic.
STREET TREE: Any tree, shrub or other woody vegetation on lands within any city
right of way. (Ord. 650-1, 3-13-2006)
7-3-4: TREE COMMITTEE:
   A.   Established: There is hereby created a St. Maries tree committee. The
St. Maries tree committee shall consist of a minimum of four (4) volunteer
members who are residents of this community. Members of the committee shall be
appointed by the mayor with the approval of the council to serve without
compensation. A city council member or employee of the city of St. Maries shall
be appointed to serve as council liaison.
   B.   Duties And Responsibilities Of Committee Members: It shall be the
responsibility of the St. Maries tree committee to:
      1.   Study, investigate, develop and update a written plan for the
selection, care, preservation, pruning, planting, replanting, removal or
disposition of trees and shrubs in the public streets and all other public
property or right of way. This plan shall constitute the official comprehensive
city tree plan for the city of St. Maries.
      2.   Distribute guidelines for the pruning of trees located on all city
properties and within city rights of way.
      3.   Distribute a tree list consisting of acceptable varieties of trees,
acceptable size of trees, proper planting and spacing instructions for trees
located within the rights of way.
      4.   Assist the city in planning and implementing Arbor Day celebrations
and activities.
      5.   Oversee planting, pruning, spraying, preserving and removal of trees
on all public properties and rights of way.
      6.   Encourage and solicit donations and other funding for the city tree
program.
   C.   Duties And Responsibilities Of Committee Chairperson: It shall be the
responsibility of the St. Maries tree committee chairperson to:
      1.   Preside over St. Maries tree committee meetings and report
activities to the liaison.
      2.   Organize materials for public education and distribution. (Ord. 650-
1, 3-13-2006)
7-3-5: AUTHORITY AND CONTROL OVER TREES:
The mayor and council have complete authority and control over all trees on or
within the city properties. The city, with advice from the tree committee may
remove or cause the removal of public or private trees or branches which create
a hazard to the public health and safety of the community. (Ord. 650-1, 3-13-
2006)
7-3-6: REMOVAL OF PUBLIC TREES AND SHRUBS:
It is the policy of the city that public trees shall not be removed without a
permit from the tree committee. Permits will be granted pursuant to the
criteria specified below:
   A.   The tree is significantly diseased, harboring injurious insects or
pathogens, is dead or near dead and constitutes a public safety hazard.
   B.   The tree interferes with overhead utility lines and creates a public
safety hazard.
   C.   The tree causes a sight obstruction in which pruning will not resolve
the problem.
   D.   Any other criteria deemed appropriate by the St. Maries tree committee.
(Ord. 650-1, 3-13-2006)
7-3-7: PLANTING OF PUBLIC TREES AND SHRUBS:
It is the policy of the city of St. Maries that public trees and shrubs shall
not be planted without a permit from the tree committee. Permits will be
granted after the committee determines the proposed location of the planting
will not interfere with overhead utility lines and will not hamper the line of
sight for traffic. (Ord. 650-1, 3-13-2006)
7-3-8: PERMIT REQUIRED:
   A.   It is unlawful to plant or remove any tree or shrub on or within the
public properties without first procuring a permit from the tree committee.
   B.   Any person desiring a permit to plant or remove a tree or shrub on or
within the city properties shall file with the city clerk or tree committee
chairperson an application to do so.
   C.   The fee for such permits shall be as established by resolution of the
city council and amended from time to time.
   D.   Upon the filing of such permit, the tree committee shall investigate
the proposed work and, if in their judgment it is desirable and should be done,
shall issue a written permit. Denial of a permit shall be issued in writing.
   E.   In addition to a permit, a temporary street closure approval from the
city is required whenever such tree work will impair the free and full use of
any sidewalk, street or alley as determined by the city public works director.
(Ord. 650-1, 3-13-2006; amd. Ord. 2023-776, 12-21-2023)
7-3-9: DAMAGING, DESTROYING OR TOPPING OF PUBLIC TREES OR SHRUBS:
It is unlawful for any person to:
   A.   Damage, mutilate or destroy any public tree or shrub of the city.
   B.   Store or place, or cause to be stored or placed: oil, gasoline,
chemicals, or any other materials harmful to trees and shrubs, around or near
public trees or shrubs.
   C.   Attach a potentially harmful device or structure (i.e., tree houses,
signs, etc.) to or on public trees unless otherwise authorized by the city.
   D.   Make excavations in the soil near roots of public trees or shrubs
unless appropriate measures are taken to prevent exposed soil from drying out.
   E.   Damage a public tree or shrub by "topping", without a permit from the
tree committee. (Ord. 650-1, 3-13-2006)
7-3-10: CARE OF TREES WITHIN THE CITY:
   A.   City Responsibilities: The city shall be responsible for the following:
      1.   Care and maintenance of park trees and shrubs.
      2.   Removal of dead, diseased or hazardous park trees, limbs, and
shrubs.
      3.   Controlling insects and diseases of park trees and shrubs.
      4.   Managing insect and disease management programs for all trees in the
city.
   B.   Private Citizens' Responsibilities: Every owner shall be responsible
for the following:
      1.   Repairing damage done to sidewalks and surrounding areas by the
roots of private trees or shrubs, or public trees and shrubs located on the
right of way adjacent to the owner's private real property.
      2.   Control of significant pests for private trees and shrubs on the
owner's private property.
      3.   Removal of any private tree or shrub which, by reason of location or
condition, constitutes an imminent danger to the health, safety or welfare of
the general public. (Ord. 650-1, 3-13-2006)
7-3-11: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any provision of this chapter is guilty of an
infraction and is subject to penalty not exceeding one hundred dollars
($100.00) as provided in subsection 1-4-1B of this code. (Ord. 650-1, 3-13-
2006)
CHAPTER 4
SPEED LIMITS
SECTIONS
7-4-1: Applicability Of State And City Regulations
7-4-2: Reasonable And Prudent Speed
7-4-3: Specific Speed Limits
7-4-4: Authority To Alter Speed Limits
7-4-1: APPLICABILITY OF STATE AND CITY REGULATIONS:
The state traffic laws regulating the speed of vehicles shall be applicable
upon all streets within the city except as in this section, as authorized by
state law, hereby declares and determines regulations shall be applicable upon
specified streets or in certain areas, in which event, it shall be unlawful for
any person to drive a vehicle at a speed in excess of any speed so declared in
this section when signs are in place giving notice thereof. (Ord. 2022-753, 1-
10-2022)
7-4-2: REASONABLE AND PRUDENT SPEED:
No person shall drive a vehicle on a street or highway within the city at speed
greater than is reasonable and prudent under the conditions and having regard
to the actual and potential hazards then existing. In every event, speed shall
be so controlled as may be necessary to avoid colliding with any person,
vehicle, or other conveyance on or entering the street or highway in compliance
with legal requirements and the duty of all persons to use due care. (Ord.
2022-753, 1-10-2022)
7-4-3: SPECIFIC SPEED LIMITS:
Except when a special hazard exists that requires lower speed for compliance
with section
7-4-2 of this chapter, the limits specified in this subsection or established
as hereinafter authorized shall be lawful speeds, and any speed in excess of
the limits specified shall be prima facie evidence that such speed is not
reasonable or prudent, and that it is unlawful.
   A.   Alleys: The speed limit shall be ten (10) miles per hour in any alley.
   B.   School Zones: The speed limit shall be fifteen (15) miles per hour when
passing any school building or when crossing any marked school zone, such zone
to extend one hundred fifty feet (150'), unless otherwise posted, in either
direction from any marked school crossing when appropriate signs giving notice
thereof are erected.
   C.   All Other Streets: The speed limit shall be twenty-five (25) miles per
hour upon all other streets in the city. (Ord. 2022-753, 1-10-2022)
7-4-4: AUTHORITY TO ALTER SPEED LIMITS:
Whenever the city council determines, on the basis of an engineering or traffic
investigation, and the residential, urban or business character of the
neighborhood abutting the street or highway in a residential, business or urban
district, that the speed limit permitted under this section is greater than is
reasonable and safe under the conditions found to exist upon a street of
highway or because of the residential, urban or business character of the
neighborhood abutting the street or highway in a residential, business or urban
district, the city council may determine and declare a reasonable and safe
maximum limit which decreases the limit within a residential, business or urban
district. (Ord. 2022-753, 1-10-2022)
TITLE 8
WATER AND SEWER
CHAPTER 1
SEWER REGULATIONS
SECTION:
8-1-1: Title
8-1-2: Definitions
8-1-3: Use Of Sewers Required
8-1-4: Private Sewage Disposal
8-1-5: Service Outside City
8-1-6: Building Sewers And Connections
8-1-7: Prohibited Discharge
8-1-8: Use Regulations
8-1-9: Protection From Damage
8-1-10: Inspectors, Power And Authority
8-1-11: Penalty
8-1-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the ST. MARIES SEWER ORDINANCE.
(1977 Code § 13.02.010)
8-1-2: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the meaning of terms used
in this chapter shall be as follows:
BOD (Denoting BIOCHEMICAL OXYGEN DEMAND): The quantity of oxygen utilized in
the biochemical oxidation or organic matter under standard laboratory procedure
in five (5) days at twenty degrees centigrade (20°C) expressed in milligrams
per liter.
BUILDING DRAIN: That part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system
which receives the discharge from soil, waste and other drainage pipes inside
the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer, beginning five
feet (5') (1.5 m) outside the inner face of the building wall.
BUILDING SEWER: The extension from the building drain to the point of
connection with the public sewer or other place of disposal.
COMBINED SEWER: A sewer receiving both surface runoff and sewage.
GARBAGE: Solid wastes from the domestic and commercial preparation, cooking and
dispensation of food, and from the handling, storage and sale of produce.
INDUSTRIAL WASTES: The liquid wastes from industrial manufacturing processes,
trade or business as distinct from sanitary sewage.
NATURAL OUTLET: Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other body
of surface or ground water.
PERSON: Any individual, firm, company, association, society, corporation or
group.
pH: The logarithm of the reciprocal of the weight of hydrogen ions in grams per
liter of solution.
PROPERLY SHREDDED GARBAGE: The wastes from the preparation, cooking and
dispensing of food that has been shredded to such a degree that all particles
will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public
sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch (1/2") (1.27 cm) in any
dimension.
PUBLIC SEWER: A sewer in which all owners of abutting properties have equal
rights, and is controlled by public authority.
SANITARY SEWER: A sewer which carries sewage and to which storm, surface and
ground waters are not intentionally admitted.
SEWAGE: A combination of the water carried wastes from residences, business
buildings, institutions and industrial establishments, together with such
ground, surface and stormwaters as may be present.
SEWAGE TREATMENT PLANT: Any arrangement of devices and structures used for
treating sewage.
SEWAGE WORKS: All facilities for collecting, dumping, treating and disposing of
sewage.
SEWER: A pipe or conduit for carrying sewage.
SHALL, MAY: "Shall" is mandatory; "may" is permissive.
SLUG: Any discharge of water, sewage, or waste which in concentration of any
given constituent or in quantity of flow exceeds for any period of duration
longer than fifteen (15) minutes more than five (5) times the average twenty
four (24) hour concentration or flows during normal operation.
STORM DRAIN (Sometimes Termed STORM SEWER): A sewer which carries storm and
surface waters and drainage, but excludes sewage and industrial wastes, other
than unpolluted cooling water.
SUPERINTENDENT: The Superintendent of Public Works of the City of St. Maries,
or his authorized deputy, agent or representative.
SUSPENDED SOLIDS: Solids that either float on the surface of, or are in
suspension in water, sewage, or other liquids, and which are removable by
laboratory filtering.
WATERCOURSE: A channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or
intermittently. (1977 Code § 13.02.020; amd. Ord. 2018-721, 5-14-2018)
8-1-3: USE OF SEWERS REQUIRED:
   A.   Prohibited Deposits: It is unlawful for any person to place, deposit,
or permit to be deposited in any unsanitary manner on public or private
property within the City or in any area under the jurisdiction of the City, any
human or animal excrement, garbage or other objectionable waste.
   B.   Prohibited Discharge: It is unlawful to discharge to any natural outlet
within the City or in any area under the jurisdiction of the City, any sewage
or other polluted waters, except where suitable treatment has been provided in
accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
   C.   Privies; Septic Tanks: Except as hereinafter provided, it shall be
unlawful to construct or maintain any privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool
or other facility intended or used for the disposal of sewage.
   D.   Toilet Facilities: The owners of all houses, buildings or properties
used for human occupancy, employment, recreation or other purposes, situated
within the City and abutting on any street, alley or right-of-way in which
there is now located or may in the future be located a public sanitary or
combined sewer of the City, is required at his expense to install suitable
toilet facilities therein, and to connect such facilities directly with the
proper public sewer in accordance with the provisions of this chapter within
ninety (90) days after date of official notice to do so, provided that said
public sewer is within one hundred feet (100') of the property line. (1977 Code
§ 13.02.030)
8-1-4: PRIVATE SEWAGE DISPOSAL:
   A.   Public System Unavailable: Where a public sanitary or combined sewer is
not available under the provisions of subsection
8-1-3D of this chapter, the building sewer shall be connected to a private
sewage disposal system complying with the provisions of this section.
   B.   Permit; Fee:
      1.   Permit Required: Before commencement of construction of a private
sewage disposal system the owner shall first obtain a written permit signed by
the Superintendent.
      2.   Application; Form: The application for such permit shall be made on
a form furnished by the City, which the applicant shall supplement by any
plans, specifications and other information as are deemed necessary by the
Superintendent.
      3.   Fee: A permit and inspection fee shall be paid to the City at the
time the application is filed. The amount of the fee shall be as established by
resolution of the city council and amended from time to time.
   C.   Permit Becomes Effective; Inspection: A permit for a private sewage
disposal system shall not become effective until the installation is completed
to the satisfaction of the Superintendent. He shall be allowed to inspect the
work at any stage of construction and, in any event, the applicant for the
permit shall notify the Superintendent when the work is ready for final
inspection and before any underground portions are covered. The inspection
shall be made within twenty four (24) hours of the receipt of notice by the
Superintendent.
   D.   Specifications Of System: The type, capacities, location and layout of
a private sewage disposal system shall comply with all recommendations of the
Idaho Department of Health and Welfare. No permit shall be issued for any
private sewage disposal system employing subsurface soil absorption facilities
where the area of the lot is less than ten thousand (10,000) square feet. No
septic tank or cesspool shall be permitted to discharge to any natural outlet.
   E.   Availability Of Public System: At such time as a public sewer becomes
available to a property served by a private sewage disposal system, as provided
in subsection D of this section, a direct connection shall be made to the
public sewer in compliance with this chapter, and any septic tanks, cesspools
and similar private sewage disposal facilities shall be abandoned and filled
with suitable material.
   F.   Operation Of Private System: The owner shall operate and maintain the
private sewage disposal facilities in a sanitary manner at all times, at no
expense to the City.
   G.   Additional Requirements: No statement contained in this section shall
be construed to interfere with any additional requirements that may be imposed
by the Health Officer.
   H.   Time Limitation: When a public sewer becomes available, the building
sewer shall be connected to said sewer within sixty (60) days and the private
sewage disposal system shall be cleaned of sludge and filled with clean bankrun
gravel or dirt. (1977 Code § 13.02.040; amd. Ord. 2023-776, 12-21-2023)
8-1-5: SERVICE OUTSIDE CITY:
The City from time to time may agree to allow access to the City sewer by users
from outside the City. By connecting on to the City sewer system, users,
whether residing within or outside the City limits, shall be deemed to have
given consent to be bound and governed by the provisions of this chapter. (1977
Code § 13.02.050)
8-1-6: BUILDING SEWERS AND CONNECTIONS:
   A.   Permit Required: No unauthorized personnel shall uncover, make any
connections with or opening into, use, alter or disturb any public sewer or
appurtenance thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the
Superintendent.
   B.   Classes Of Permits; Application: There shall be two (2) classes of
building sewer permits: 1) for residential and commercial service, and 2) for
service to establishments producing industrial wastes. In either case, the
owner or his agent shall make application on a special form furnished by the
City. The permit application shall be supplemented by any plans, specifications
or other information considered pertinent in the judgment of the
Superintendent.
   C.   Permit And Inspection Fee: A permit and inspection fee for a sewer
permit shall be paid to the City at the time the application is filed. The
permit and inspection fee shall be as established by resolution of the city
council and amended from time to time.
   D.   Costs; Indemnification:
      1.   Connection To Curb: The City shall provide the connection mechanism
and the service pipe from the City sewer main to the curb, or at the discretion
of the City, to the lot line of the property to be served provided the distance
is not greater than seventy five feet (75'). The owner of the property to be
served shall bear the expense of installing the connection mechanism and the
service pipe.
      2.   All Other Costs: All pipe in excess of seventy five feet (75') or
extending beyond the curb or the lot line, shall be paid for by the owner of
the property served. Any additional costs and expenses incident to the
installation and connection of the building sewer shall be borne by the owner.
      3.   Indemnity: The owner shall indemnify the City from any loss or
damage that may directly or indirectly be occasioned by the installation of the
building sewer.
   E.   Breaks Or Blockages:
      1.   The City will be responsible for repair to breaks or blockages that
occur to the public sewer main.
      2.   The property owner will be responsible for breaks or blockages that
occur to the building sewer.
      3.   Where there is a break or blockage and it is doubtful whether the
break or blockage is located on the public sewer main or in the building sewer,
the City shall have the charge of the repairs but the cost of the repairs shall
be assessed to the private property owner in the event the break or blockage is
in the building sewer.
   F.   Cleanout Boxes: For all new construction, the owner shall be required
to install a cleanout in the lateral pipe at the lot line.
   G.   Separate Sewers Required; Exception: A separate and independent
building sewer shall be provided for every building; except where one building
stands at the rear of another on an interior lot and no private sewer is
available or can be constructed to the rear building through an adjoining
alley, court, yard or driveway, the building sewer from the front building may
be extended to the rear building and the whole considered as one building
sewer. Each building shall have its own connection to the City sewer main.
   H.   Existing Building Sewers: Old building sewers may be used in connection
with new buildings only when they are found, on examination and test by the
Superintendent, to meet all requirements of this chapter.
   I.   Specifications: The size, slope, alignment, materials of construction
of a building sewer and the methods to be used in excavating, placing of the
pipe, jointing, testing and backfilling the trench shall all conform to the
requirements of the Building and Plumbing Codes or other applicable rules and
regulations of the City. In the absence of code provisions or in amplification
thereof, the materials and procedures set forth in appropriate specifications
of the ASTM and WPCF Manual of Practice No. 9 shall apply.
   J.   Elevation: Whenever possible the building sewer shall be brought to the
building at an elevation below the basement floor. In all buildings in which
any building main is too low to permit gravity flow to the public sewer,
sanitary sewage carried by such building drain shall be lifted by an approved
means and discharged to the building sewer.
   K.   Storm Drainage Prohibited: No person shall make connection of roof
downspouts, exterior foundation drains, areaway drains or other sources of
surface runoff of groundwater to a building sewer or building drain which in
turn is connected directly or indirectly to a public sanitary sewer.
   L.   Compliance Required: The connection of the building sewer shall conform
to the requirements of the Building and Plumbing Codes or other applicable
rules and regulations of the City, or the procedures set forth in appropriate
specifications of the ASTM and the WPCF Manual of Practice No. 9. All such
connections shall be made gastight and watertight. Any deviation from the
prescribed procedures and materials must be approved by the Superintendent
before installation.
   M.   Inspection; Connection: The applicant for the building sewer permit
shall notify the Superintendent when the building sewer is ready for inspection
and connection to the public sewer. The inspection shall be done prior to fill
being placed over the connection and sewer line. The connection shall be made
under the supervision of the Superintendent or his representative.
   N.   Excavations: All excavations for building sewer installation shall be
adequately guarded with barricades and lights so as to protect the public from
hazard. Streets, sidewalks, parkways and other public property disturbed in the
course of the work shall be restored in a manner satisfactory to the City. The
owner shall bear the cost of restoring the streets, sidewalks, parkways and
other public property. (Ord. 2018-721, 5-14-2018; amd. Ord. 2023-776, 12-21-
2023)
8-1-7: PROHIBITED DISCHARGE:
   A.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any stormwater,
surface water, groundwater, roof runoff, subsurface drainage, uncontaminated
cooling water or unpolluted industrial process waters to any sanitary sewer.
   B.   Stormwater and all other unpolluted drainage shall be discharged to
such sewers as are specifically designated as combined sewers or storm sewers,
or to a natural outlet approved by the Superintendent. Industrial cooling water
or unpolluted process waters may be discharged, on approval of the
Superintendent, to a storm sewer, combined sewer or natural outlet.
   C.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the
following waters or wastes to any public sewers:
      1.   Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil or other flammable or
explosive liquid, solid or gas;
      2.   Any waters or wastes containing toxic or poisonous solids, liquids
or gasses in sufficient quantity, singly or by interaction with other wastes to
injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process, constitute a hazard to
humans or animals, create a public nuisance, or create any hazard in the
receiving waters of the sewage treatment plant, including, but not limited to,
cyanides in excess of two milligrams per liter (2 mg/L) as CN in the wastes as
discharged to the public sewer;
      3.   Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5 or having any other
corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard to structures, equipment
and personnel of the sewage works;
      4.   Solid or viscous substances in quantities or of such size capable of
causing obstruction to the flow in sewers, or other interference with the
proper operation of the sewage works, such as but not limited to, ashes,
cinders, sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags, feathers, tar,
plastics, wood, unground garbage, whole blood, paunch manure, hair and
fleshings, entrails and paper dishes, cups, milk containers, etc., either whole
or ground by garbage grinders.
   D.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged the following
described substances, materials, water or wastes if it appears likely in the
opinion of the superintendent that such wastes can harm either the sewers,
sewage treatment process, or equipment, have an adverse effect on the receiving
stream, or can otherwise endanger life, limb, public property, or constitute a
nuisance. In forming his opinion as to the acceptability of these wastes, the
superintendent will give the consideration to such factors as to quantities of
subject wastes in relation to flows and velocities in the sewers, materials of
construction of the sewers, nature of the sewage treatment process, the sewers,
capacity of the sewage treatment plant, degree of treatability of wastes in the
sewage treatment plant, and other pertinent factors. The substances prohibited
are:
      1.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred
fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F) (65°C);
      2.   Any water or waste containing fats, wax, grease or oils, emulsified
or not, in excess of one hundred (100) mg/l or containing substances which may
solidify or become viscous at temperatures between thirty two degrees
Fahrenheit (32°F) and one hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F) (0° and
65°C);
      3.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. The installation
and operation of any garbage grinder with a motor three-fourths (3/4)
horsepower or greater shall be subject to review and approval of the
superintendent;
      4.   Any waters or wastes containing strong acid iron pickling wastes or
concentrated plating solutions, whether neutralized or not;
      5.   Any waters or wastes containing iron, chromium, copper, zinc, and
similar objectionable or toxic substances; or wastes exerting an excessive
chlorine requirement, to such degree that any such material received in the
composite sewage at the sewage treatment works exceeds the limits established
by the superintendent for such materials;
      6.   Any waters or wastes containing phenols or other taste producing or
odor producing substances, in such concentrations exceeding limits which may be
established by the superintendent as necessary, after treatment of the
composite sewage, to meet the requirements of the state, federal or other
public agencies or jurisdiction for such discharge to the receiving waters;
      7.   Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such halflife or
concentrations as may exceed limits established by the superintendent in
compliance with applicable state or federal regulations;
      8.   Any waters or wastes having a pH in excess of nine and five- tenths
(9.5);
      9.   Materials which exert or cause:
         a.   Unusual concentrations of inert suspended solids, such as, but
not limited to, fullers earth, lime slurries, and lime residues, or of
dissolved solids, such as, but not limited to, sodium chloride or sodium
sulfate;
         b.   Excessive discoloration, such as, but not limited to, dye wastes
and vegetable tanning solutions;
         c.   Unusual BOD, chemical oxygen demand, or chlorine requirements in
such quantities as to constitute a significant load on the sewage treatment
works;
         d.   Unusual volume of flow or concentrations of wastes constituting
"slugs" as defined in section
8-1-2 of this chapter;
      10.   Waters or wastes containing substances which are not amenable to
treatment or reduction by the sewage treatment processes employed, or are
amenable to treatment only to such degree that the sewage treatment plant
effluent cannot meet the requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction
over discharge to the receiving waters. (1977 Code § 13.02.070)
8-1-8: USE REGULATIONS:
   A.   Power Of Superintendent: If any waters or wastes are discharged or are
proposed to be discharged to the public sewers, which waters contain the
substances or possess the characteristics enumerated in subsection
8-1-7D of this chapter, and which in the judgment of the superintendent may
have a deleterious effect upon the sewage works, processes, equipment, or
receiving waters, or which otherwise create a hazard to life or constitute a
public nuisance, the superintendent may:
      1.   Reject the wastes;
      2.   Require pretreatment to an acceptable condition for discharge to the
public sewers;
      3.   Require control over the quantities and rates of discharge; and/or
      4.   Require payment to cover the added cost of handling and treating the
wastes not covered by existing taxes or sewer charge under the provision of
subsection F of this section.
If the superintendent permits the pretreatment or equalization of water flows,
the design and installation of the plants and equipment shall be subject to the
review and approval of the superintendent and subject to the requirements of
all applicable codes, ordinances and laws.
   B.   Interceptors: Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided when,
in the opinion of the superintendent, they are necessary for the proper
handling of liquid wastes containing grease in excessive amounts, or any
flammable wastes, sand or other harmful ingredients; except that such
interceptors shall not be required for private living quarters or dwelling
units. All interceptors shall be of a type and capacity approved by the
superintendent and shall be located as to be readily and easily accessible for
cleaning and inspection.
   C.   Pretreatment: Where preliminary treatment or flow equalizing facilities
are provided for any waters or wastes, they shall be maintained continuously in
satisfactory and effective operation by the owner at his expense.
   D.   Control Manhole: When required by the superintendent, the owner of any
property serviced by a building sewer carrying industrial wastes shall install
a suitable control manhole together with such necessary meters and other
appurtenances in the building sewer to facilitate observation, sampling and
measurement of the wastes. Such manhole, when required, shall be accessibly and
safely located, and shall be constructed in accordance with plans approved by
the superintendent. The manhole shall be installed by the owner at his expense,
and shall be maintained by him so as to be safe and accessible at all times.
   E.   Measurements, Tests And Analysis: All measurements, tests and analyses
of the characteristics of waters and wastes to which reference is made in this
chapter shall be determined in accordance with the latest edition of "Standard
Methods For The Examination Of Water And Wastewater", published by the American
Public Health Association, and shall be determined at the control manhole
provided, or upon suitable samples taken at said control manhole. In the event
that no special manhole has been required, the control manhole shall be
considered to be the nearest downstream manhole in the public sewer to the
point at which the building sewer is connected. Sampling shall be carried out
by customarily accepted methods to reflect the effect of constituents upon the
sewage works and to determine the existence of hazards to life, limb and
property. (The particular analyses involved will determine whether a 24-hour
composite of all outfalls of a premises is appropriate or whether a grab sample
or samples should be taken. Normally, but not always, BOD and suspended solids
analyses are obtained from 24-hour composites of all outfalls whereas pHs are
determined from periodic grab samples.)
   F.   Special Agreement: No statement contained in this section shall be
construed as preventing any special agreement or arrangement between the city
and any industrial concern whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or
character may be accepted by the city for treatment, subject to payment
therefor, by the industrial concern. (1977 Code § 13.02.070)
8-1-9: PROTECTION FROM DAMAGE:
No unauthorized person shall maliciously, wilfully or negligently break,
damage, destroy, uncover, deface or tamper with any structure, appurtenance or
equipment which is a part of the sewage works. Any person violating this
provision shall be subject to immediate arrest under charge of disorderly
conduct. (1977 Code § 13.02.080)
8-1-10: INSPECTORS, POWER AND AUTHORITY:
   A.   Permitted Entry: The superintendent and other duly authorized employees
of the city bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to
enter all properties for the purposes of inspection, observation, measurement,
sampling and testing in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
   B.   Inquiry To Processes: The superintendent or his representatives shall
have no authority to inquire into any processes including metallurgical,
chemical, oil, refining, ceramic, paper or other industries beyond that point
having a direct bearing on the kind and sources of discharge to the sewers or
waterways or facilities for waste treatment.
   C.   Safety Rules: While performing the necessary work on private properties
referred to in subsection A of this section, the superintendent or duly
authorized employees of the city shall observe all safety rules applicable to
the premises established by the company and the company shall be held harmless
for injury or death to the city employees and the city shall indemnify the
company against loss or damage to its property by city employees and against
liability claims and demands for personal injury or property damage asserted
against the company and growing out of the gauging and sampling operation,
except as such may be caused by negligence or failure of the company to
maintain safe conditions as required in subsection 8-1-8D of this chapter.
   D.   Entry To Easement: The superintendent and other duly authorized
employees of the city bearing property credentials and identification shall be
permitted to enter all private properties through which the city holds a duly
negotiated easement for the purpose of, but not limited to, inspection,
observation, measurement, sampling, repair and maintenance of any portion of
the sewage works lying within said easement. All entry and subsequent work, if
any, on said easement, shall be done in full accordance with the terms of the
duly negotiated easement pertaining to the private property involved. (1977
Code § 13.02.090)
8-1-11: PENALTY:
   A.   Notice Of Violation: Any person found to be violating any provision of
this chapter, except section
8-1-9, shall be served by the city with written notice stating the nature of
the violation and providing a reasonable time limit for the satisfactory
correction thereof. The offender shall, within the period of time stated in
such notice, permanently cease all violations.
   B.   Failure To Comply: Any person who shall continue any violation beyond
the time limit provided for in subsection A of this section, shall be guilty of
a misdemeanor, and on conviction thereof shall be fined in the amount not
exceeding one hundred dollars ($100.00) per day for each violation. Each day in
which such violations shall continue shall be deemed a separate offense.
   C.   Liability For Damage: Any person violating any of the provisions of
this chapter shall become liable to the city for any expense, loss or damage
occasioned by the city by reason of such violation. (1977 Code § 13.02.100)
CHAPTER 2
SEWER RATES
SECTION:
8-2-1: Title
8-2-2: Purpose
8-2-3: Applicability
8-2-4: Minimum Rates
8-2-5: Reserved
8-2-6: Periodic Review
8-2-7: Annual Notification
8-2-8: Retained Authority
8-2-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the CITY SEWER RATE ORDINANCE.
(1977 Code § 13.06.010)
8-2-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter shall be to provide for the health of the residents
of the city by providing for the means by which the city's sanitary sewer
system may be adequately operated and maintained. (1977 Code § 13.06.020)
8-2-3: APPLICABILITY:
The rates prescribed in this chapter shall apply to all structures, homes and
buildings or other units wherein an independent sewer connection is in use; all
dwellings and structures designed for human occupancy shall be deemed to be
user units within the meaning of this section. (1977 Code § 13.06.030)
8-2-4: MINIMUM RATES:
   A.   Inside City Limits: The basic minimum rate for sewer services furnished
by the city to sewer service users within the city shall be established by
resolution of the city council and amended from time to time.
   B.   Outside City Limits: The minimum rate for residential sewer service and
other sewer service outside the city limits of the city shall be established by
resolution of the city council and amended from time to time. (1977 Code §§
13.06.040 and 13.06.050; amd. 2004 Code; Ord. 2023-776, 12-21-2023)
8-2-5: RESERVED:
Reserved by Ord. 2023-776, 12-21-2023.
8-2-6: PERIODIC REVIEW:
The city shall conduct a periodic review of the rate basis for establishing
sewer user charges and the rate schedules as provided herein and as per adopted
user charge system shall be revised from time to time as may be indicated by
each periodic review. Periodic reviews shall be conducted no less frequently
then biannually. (1977 Code § 13.06.070)
8-2-7: ANNUAL NOTIFICATION:
The city shall, on an annual basis, notify each user of that portion of the
user charge attributable to wastewater treatment services. (1977 Code §
13.06.080)
8-2-8: RETAINED AUTHORITY:
These rates may be changed or altered at any time by resolution of the city
council or by amendment of this chapter as in the opinion of the city council
such change is deemed advisable. (1977 Code § 13.06.090)
CHAPTER 3
WATER REGULATIONS
ARTICLE A. GENERAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
8-3A-1: Supervision
8-3A-2: Application For Tapping And Connection Permit
8-3A-3: Installation And Maintenance Of Equipment
8-3A-4: Excavations
8-3A-5: Shutoff Permitted
8-3A-1: SUPERVISION:
   A.   The public works directors shall be the head of the water department
and subject only to the orders of the city council. The public works directors
shall perform the duties herein prescribed for the water department of the
city, except such duties as may be specifically assigned to the city treasurer
as the clerk of the water department. (1977 Code § 13.08.010)
   B.   The water department shall consist of the city treasurer as clerk of
the water department, and the public works directors, who shall carry out all
the provisions of this chapter and shall be subject only in matters of
discretion to the city council. (1977 Code § 13.08.020)
8-3A-2: APPLICATION FOR TAPPING AND CONNECTION PERMIT:
   A.   Applicant: All applications for the tapping or connection with any
water mains must be made at the office of the water department by the owner of
the property to be served, or their legal agents.
   B.   Required Information: The applicant shall fully state all purposes for
which the water is required, the size and number of taps or other outlets from
which the water is to be drawn, and the number of the lot and block to which
the water is to be taken and used and the street from which it is desired that
the service pipe shall be laid.
   C.   Rules And Regulations: Such application shall show upon its face that
the same is made, taken and accepted subject to any and all rules and
regulations then in force, or to be made later, for the government and control
of the waterworks system.
   D.   Connection By City: No person other than an authorized employee of the
city shall tap or make any perforation or opening of any kind in any water main
or any service pipe from which water may be taken. (1977 Code § 13.08.070)
8-3A-3: INSTALLATION AND MAINTENANCE OF EQUIPMENT:
   A.   Service Pipe:
      1.   City To Bear Cost: The water department will, at the expense of the
city, run a service pipe not larger than three-fourths of an inch (3/4") from
the city water main to the lot line of any applicant or consumer of water;
provided, that the distance is not greater than seventy five feet (75').
      2.   Owner To Bear Cost: All pipe in excess of seventy five feet (75') in
length, or three-fourths of an inch (3/4") in size, is to be laid by and under
the direction of the city water department, and the expense thereof charged to
the consumer or owner of the property served.
   B.   Owner/Consumer Responsibility: The water consumer, or the owner of the
property served, shall at all times be responsible for the condition of the
lateral pipes, curb cock and box when located on his premises, and such owner,
or water consumer, shall be responsible for all damages resulting from leaks or
breaks to the service pipe on his property; and no claim shall be made against
the city on account of the breaking of any service pipe or apparatus, or for
the failure in the supply of water.
   C.   City Responsibility: The city will be responsible for repair of leaks
that occur upon public property.
   D.   Break Or Leak: If a water user notifies the city of a water leak within
fifteen (15) days of the last billing, the city will recalculate that month's
billing by averaging the last three (3) months' charges and crediting the
remaining usage. Prompt repair of the water leak by the property owner is
required. If repair is not completed by the next billing period, full charges
will resume.
      1.   Responsibility To Repair: Where a break or leak occurs in a lateral
service pipe, the property owner or water consumer will be required to repair
the pipes at his own expense and to protect the city and the water department
from any cost for such repair.
      2.   Failure To Repair: If, after being notified, the owner of the
property upon which a break or leak occurs or his agent does not make the
necessary repairs to his lateral service pipe immediately, the water department
shall cause the water to be shut off from said premises and the same shall not
be turned on until the service pipe has been properly repaired and the owner or
water consumer has paid to the city the fee for the shutting off and turning on
of said water. Said fee shall be as established by resolution of the city
council and amended from time to time.
      3.   Liability For Damages: Where a break or leak occurs in a lateral
service pipe, the property owner or water consumer shall be responsible for any
and all damages resulting therefrom.
      4.   Location Of Break Uncertain: Where there is a leak and it is
doubtful whether the water is from a break in the city main or in a private
service pipe or lateral line, the city shall have charge of the repairs but the
costs of repairs shall be assessed to the proper private property owner or
consumer in the event the leak or break is in a service pipe or lateral line.
(1977 Code § 13.08.030; amd. 2004 Code; Ord. 649, 4-10-2006; Ord. 2023-776, 12-
21-2023)
8-3A-4: EXCAVATIONS:
   A.   Permit Required: Before excavation within the streets, for the purpose
of laying service pipes or repairing the same, the owners of property to be
served, or their legal agent, must first, through the plumber doing the work or
by themselves, secure a permit for such work from the office of the city clerk
on a form provided for that purpose. (1977 Code § 13.08.060)
   B.   Safety Precautions: The streets must be opened in the manner which will
occasion the least inconvenience to the public. No excavation in any street or
alley shall be left open overnight unless properly guarded with rails and red
lights, which must be maintained from sunset to sunrise; and every precaution
must be taken to ensure public safety. (1977 Code § 13.08.050)
8-3A-5: SHUTOFF PERMITTED:
The water department reserves the right at any time to shut off, without
notice, the water from its main for the purpose of making repairs or
extensions, or for any other purpose; and no claim shall be made against the
city by reason of the breakage of any service pipe or from any other damage
that may result from shutting off said water. (1977 Code § 13.08.040)
ARTICLE B. WATER CONNECTIONS
SECTION:
8-3B-1: Title
8-3B-2: Connection Required; Billing
8-3B-3: Connection Fee
8-3B-4: Notice Of Violation
8-3B-1: TITLE:
This article shall be known and may be cited as the CITY OF ST. MARIES WATER
CONNECTION ORDINANCE. (1977 Code § 13.10.010)
8-3B-2: CONNECTION REQUIRED; BILLING:
   A.   Connection Required: The owners of all houses, buildings or properties
used for human occupancy, employment, recreation or other purpose, situated
within the city shall and they are required to install all suitable water
facilities therein, and to connect such facilities directly with the public
water system of the city, provided that such water system is located where it
is possible or practicable for such owner to make such connection, whether such
property be located within a local improvement district or elsewhere. The
practicability of connection shall be determined by the city council.
   B.   Uninterrupted Billing: A monthly basic rate water bill will be
generated at month end and every month subsequently following the purchase of a
water hookup regardless if the tap has or has not been made into the main line.
Once a service connection has been established, a monthly bill will be
generated regardless if it is in use or not in use. Water service may not be
temporarily shut off in order to avoid paying a monthly base rate charge. (Ord.
2008-662, 9-8-2008, eff. 10-1-2008)
8-3B-3: CONNECTION FEE:
Such owner, upon making such water connection with the public water system as
required in this article, whenever a connection from the main line to the
property is required to be installed, shall pay the appropriate and proper fee
therefor, which fee shall from time to time be set by resolution of the mayor
and city council under the terms of existing rules and regulations and
ordinances of the city whether such property be located within an existing
local improvement district within the city or elsewhere. (1977 Code §
13.10.030)
8-3B-4: NOTICE OF VIOLATION:
Any person found to be violating the provisions of this article shall be served
by the city with written notice of same stating the nature of the violation,
and providing a reasonable time for satisfactory correction thereof, such time
to be determined by the city council. The offender shall, within the period of
time stated in such notice, cease the violation of this article by paying the
proper fee or otherwise. (1977 Code § 13.10.040)
ARTICLE C. INSTALLATION REGULATIONS
SECTION:
8-3C-1: Water Meters
8-3C-2: Service Outside City Limits
8-3C-1: WATER METERS:
   A.   Required:
      1.   All commercial property owners within the corporate limits of the
city and all commercial property owners located outside the corporate limits of
the city who are purchasers of city water under the terms and conditions set
forth by the city, including all commercial property owners where city water is
supplied by the city, in, on or upon premises where water is consumed by the
owner, tenant, occupant, customer or otherwise, shall have a water meter
installed. Such water meter shall be purchased and installed at the expense of
the city and approved by and through the city public works department. It shall
be installed at and upon the respective commercial premises not later than
January 1, 2007; or in a time frame favorable to the public works department,
and all city water used in, on or upon said commercial premises shall pass
through and be measured by such water meter. In the event that any commercial
property owner shall refuse to allow the city to install a water meter on or
before January 1, 2007, or in a time frame favorable to the public works
department, or shall fail to pay as required, it shall be the duty of the
public works department to discontinue the water service to the premises or
property of such commercial property owner, or to refuse to deliver water to
the property or premises of the owner.
   B.   Type Of Meter: All meters installed in or outside the corporate limits
of the city for the purpose of measuring city water shall be water meters
approved by the public works department.
   C.   Placement: Meters shall be set at the point where the service pipe
enters the property, as near to the property line as possible and at a place
easily accessible or upon the recommendation of placement by the city public
works department. All meters must be placed in a meter box approved by the
public works department and sufficiently large enough to permit removal or
resetting of the meter. The enclosure must be frostproof with a secure lid. A
removable insulated cover to prevent cold air from reaching the meter is
required. If determined necessary by the public works department, a backflow
prevention assembly approved by the public works department shall be purchased
by the property owner and installed at the expense of the property owner in
accordance with chapter 5 of this title. The backflow prevention assembly will
be maintained by the property owner, and it will be the property owner's
responsibility to repair the backflow assembly in the event of damage due to
injury or frost.
   D.   Ownership And Maintenance; Liability For Damage: Consumers supplied by
meter shall take every reasonable precaution to protect the meter and all
appurtenances, i.e., meter set, enclosure, pressure reducing valve (if
required), from injury or damage by frost or otherwise. The meter shall be the
property of the city and the city shall be liable for all repair or replacement
to said meters and appurtenances excluding backflow assembly.
   E.   Failure To Register Correctly; Testing: If from any cause the meter
fails to register correctly, the charge to the consumer shall be at the rate
used for the corresponding period of the month previous, or if for any reason
the rate for the corresponding period of the previous month cannot be justly
applied, the rate shall be equitably adjusted by the utility clerk. (Ord. 649,
4-10-2006)
8-3C-2: SERVICE OUTSIDE CITY LIMITS:
   A.   City Council Authority: From and after the effective date hereof, it
shall be discretionary with the city council as to whether water service shall
be provided outside the corporate limits of the city.
   B.   Hookup Charge: From and after the effective date hereof, a minimum
hookup charge as set from time to time by resolution of the city council shall
be made and collected in all instances where water services are to be provided
outside the corporate limits of the city, which fee shall be paid in advance to
the city clerk. (Ord. 649, 4-10-2006)
ARTICLE D. WATER RATES
SECTION:
8-3D-1: Authority
8-3D-2: Applicability
8-3D-3: Minimum Rates
8-3D-4: Unmetered Premises
8-3D-5: Separate Service Required; Exception
8-3D-6: Shutoff Orders
8-3D-7: Use For Building Purposes
8-3D-8: Analysis Fee
8-3D-1: AUTHORITY:
The city, through the mayor and city council, retains authority to make any
amendment to or additions or corrections to the following rates by city council
action or by resolution, and specifically retains the right to enter into
contract or agreement with respect to revised water rates with any water
district which may in the future be formed outside the city limits. (1977 Code
§ 13.16.170)
8-3D-2: APPLICABILITY:
The rates prescribed in this article shall apply to all structures, homes and
buildings or other units wherein an independent water connection is in use; all
dwellings and structures designed for human occupancy shall be deemed to be
user units within the meaning of this article. (1977 Code § 13.16.130)
8-3D-3: MINIMUM RATES:
The minimum rates, as established by resolution of the city council and amended
from time to time, shall be for use up to the sum of twelve thousand (12,000)
gallons per month or lesser amount of water consumed in such structure or
premises. Payment and collection of rates is provided for in
chapter 4 of this title. (Ord. 2009-668, 1-26-2009; amd. Ord. 2023-776, 12-21-
2023)
8-3D-4: UNMETERED PREMISES:
   A.   Schedule Of Estimated Use: With respect to structures and premises
wherein water use is not metered, the water rates will be charged on the basis
of estimated water use in accordance with the following schedule:

   B.   Premises Not Included In Schedule: For any establishment or premises
not specifically listed above, an agreement shall be arrived at between the
city and the owner or occupant of such premises, structure or establishment as
to the estimated amount of use, or a meter shall be installed at the cost of
